API Documentation Overview

Welcome on the GRID

GRID provides competitive gaming data through APIs. The data is split up in:

Static data: schedules, tournaments, teams, ...

In-game data: gameplay data, updated as a series is played

The documentation is here to:

Help you interact with our APIs as quickly as possible

Go to our Static Data Quick-Start Guide

Go to our In-Game Data Quick-Start Guide

Explain how our APIs are designed

Provide you with a complete view of what is available

Go to our API Reference

Use the table of contents on the left to explore further.

Access

An authorised API key is required to gain access to each GraphQL API by setting the x-api-key header on each POST request. If you do not have an API key, or have any other questions around access, please contact our Support Team.

Discover

To interact and discover what is available via GRID APIs, the following development tools are maintained.

GraphQL Playground

GraphQL is a language that enables a flexible approach to querying APIs, by enabling the client to query only what is required. Most APIs offered as part of the GRID data feeds are queryable with GraphQL.

In order to discover and test different GraphQL queries across these APIs, the GraphQL Playground is available that allows live queries for real data. It is possible to view the schema for each API using the panel located on the right-hand side of the playground application.

Data Feed Viewer

The Data Feed Viewer enables consumers to discover the events data contained within transactions, published by the Series Events API.

Get Support

If you have any questions or require support using GRID's APIs, please reach out to our Support Team.

Glossary

This document provides definitions for GRID-specific, competitive gaming, software development, and gaming terminology, which might be unfamiliar to the reader.

The definitions are grouped per category.

Competitive gaming

Term

Definition

Title

A competitive video game title.

Player

A singular player competing in a title.

Team

A collection of players competing in a title.

Game

A singular, in-game matchup between teams.

Map

A virtual environment in which a game takes place.

Character

A virtual character controlled by a player and located on the map during a game.

Series

A matchup between teams, consisting of one or more consecutive games.

Tournament

A competition, consisting of multiple series between teams.

Scrim

A practice or training match between two teams.

Esports

A form of competitive video gaming that involves professional players and teams competing in organized tournaments or leagues.

General

Term

Definition

In-game

Simulated by a title's game engine.

State

The in-game situation.

Event

Something that happens in-game.

GRID

Term

Definition

Entities

A real-world object or concept that is represented by a set of data fields or attributes that define its properties and characteristics.

Format

The format of a series determines the number of games played and how the winner is determined. For example, BO1 and BO3 formats, respectively, "best-of-1" and "best-of-3", indicate that one or up to three games are played. The winner of a BO1 series wins with one game, and the winner of a BO3 series wins with two games.

Service Level

The service level indicates the type of coverage GRID offers for a given series in each product. The value of this field can be FULL, LIMITED and NONE.

Product

A service or API provided by GRID.

Video Stream

A video of the series that is being played.

Score Advantage

Score advantage indicates either of the following scenarios:

Loopfeed

A test series that gets repeated over and over.

Title-agnostic

Something that is not handled differently per title.

Segment

Section of a game or another segment, such as a round.

Objective

An important in-game achievement.

Software development

Term

Definition

REST

REST API (Representational State Transfer Application Programming Interface) is a type of web API that uses HTTP requests to access and manipulate data, typically using JSON or XML formats.

GraphQL

GraphQL is a query language and runtime for APIs that enables clients to request only the data they need.

WebSocket

A WebSocket is a communication protocol that enables bi-directional, real-time, and persistent connections between a client and a server over a single TCP socket.

API Key

A secret token that is passed to the API to identify the caller and authorize their access to the API's features and data.

Gaming terminology

Term

Definition

Money

In-game currency used to obtain items and advantages during the game.

Inventory Value

The value of all of the items a player has purchased during a game.

Kill

The act of dropping a character to zero health, usually getting a monetary reward.

Death

The event of a character dropping to zero health, usually meaning a disadvantage to the team, such as respawn time or inability to keep playing a round.

Assist

The act of collaborating in killing a player, usually resulting in a smaller monetary reward.

Item

An object that a player can buy in-game that might give them extra stats.

Ability

A special move or power a player can use in-game, often character-specific.

Streak

The number of characters in a row a player was able to kill.

Title-specific terminology

Valorant

Valorant is a first-person tactical hero shooter developed and published by Riot Games.

Term

Definition

Spike

A bomb-like device that agents plant/defuse. It is one of the ways a team has to win rounds.

Attackers

The team whose objective is to plant the spike in an enemy site.

Defenders

The team whose objective is to prevent the enemies from planting the spike, defending their sites.

Agents

A character in Valorant.

Buyphase

Period of time during a game when players can purchase weapons, shields, and abilities using a currency that is based on their performance in the previous round.

CSGO

Counter-Strike: Global Offensive (CS:GO) is a multiplayer first-person shooter game developed by Valve and Hidden Path Entertainment.

Term

Definition

Grenades

A type of weapon that can be bought by players. Using it removes it from the inventory.

Bomb

A bomb-like device that players plant/defuse. It is one of the ways a team has to win rounds.

Freezetime

Period of time during a game when players can purchase items using a currency that is based on their performance in the previous round.

Terrorists

The team whose objective is to plant the bomb.

Counter-terrorists

The team whose objective is to prevent enemies from planting the bomb.

DOTA

Dota 2 is a 2013 multiplayer online battle arena (MOBA) video game developed by Valve Corporation.

Term

Definition

Roshan

Roshan, is the most powerful neutral creep in Dota 2. Provides a buff to the team that kills it. It’s one of the objectives tracked by the Series Events API.

Radiant

One of the sides in DOTA, in-game, the bottom left half of the game map belongs to the Radiant.

Dire

One of the sides in DOTA, in-game, the top right half of the game map belongs to the Dire.

Hero

A character in DOTA.

Understanding the results

The output of the GetCsgoLoopfeedSeries query provides static data for the CSGO Loopfeed series (a demo CSGO series running cyclically on the GRID Platform). The following key data points are included:

Series: the parent entity. Note that a series may contain other entities within it. Our query shows that this series has an ID, which can be used to identify it in the GRID Data Platform.

startTimeScheduled: indicates the scheduled start time of the series. In this example, the series begins on the 18th of November at 13:34hs.

format: specifies how many games are included in the series and how the winner will be determined. In this example, the series is a "best of three" (Bo3), which means up to three games will be played.

Title: the title refers to the game being played. One of the title data points is nameShortened, which is a commonly used abbreviation for the game. In this example, the title is CSGO, or Counter-Strike: Global Offensive. Note that the title's full name and the GRID ID can also be requested as part of the query.

Tournament: the tournament provides context for where a series is being played. In this example, as this is a test series, the tournament is GRID-TEST. However, in real series, you can find tournaments such as The Champion of Champions Tour.

Teams: the teams show who will be playing in the game.

baseInfo: provides some of the most relevant information about a team. We obtain the team’s name in the example, but additional data points are available.

scoreAdvantage: a team can start a series with a game advantage. In the example, none of the teams has an advantage.

Additional Resources

The example includes only some of the GRID Central Data Feed's data points. Please refer to the GraphQL API Schema documentation for a comprehensive list of the available data points. The Schema documentation can be accessed by clicking the Docs button in the GraphQL Playground.

Static Data Overview

The Central Data Feed is the repository of GRID's static data.

The term "static data" refers to information regarding an entity not associated with in-game data.

For instance, data points related to a team, such as its name, logo, branding colors, and the title in which they compete, are considered static data.

These data points remain constant during a series and are not affected by any in-game events; thus, GRID categorizes them as static data.

Central Data URLs

There are two URLs that can be used to access Central Data. One is for Open Access users and the other is for clients with commercial level access.

Open Access URL

https://api-op.grid.gg/central-data/graphql

Full Access URL

https://api.grid.gg/central-data/graphql

Static Data Entities

Players, teams, titles, tournaments, and series are the primary entities in the Central Data Feed.

Relationships

Entities in the Central Data Feed are interconnected and can be represented as nodes in a graph. The relationship between entities is denoted by edges (see GraphQL connections), with additional information about the relationship included in the relationship fields (e.g. scoreAdvantage for a team participant relationship on the series entity).

For instance, in the context of a best-of-three series between C9 White and G2 Gozen for Valorant Game Changers, a Series entity can be linked to several other entities to obtain their respective data.

Players

Players represent the individuals participating in games. This entity is used in the Live Data to keep track of players between different matches consistently.

Teams

Teams identify groups of players participating in games.

Related entity: Team Participant

This entity can be found in Series, and has the information of the team, alongside the score advantage for a given series.

Titles

Titles describe the games supported by GRID. For example, Valorant, CSGO and DotA are some of the supported titles. They play an important role in defining the Live Data Feed. While all the GRID APIs are title-agnostic, events and states may have small differences between titles to express the game state fully.

Tournaments

Tournaments are competitions in which teams participate.

Series

A Series represents a minimum of one game played by two teams in a tournament context. The Series entity in the Central Data Feed does not track in-game events but instead records data points related to scheduling, context, and format.

Related entity: Series Format

The format of a series determines the number of games played and how the winner is determined. For example, BO1 and BO3 formats, respectively, "best-of-1" and "best-of-3", indicate that one or up to three games are played. The winner of a BO1 series wins with one game, and the winner of a BO3 series wins with two games.

Related entity: Product Service Level

The service level indicates the type of coverage GRID offers for a given series in each product. The value of this field can be FULL, LIMITED and NONE.

Related entity: Video Stream

The video stream entity provides the URL for a series's live video stream.

Static Data FAQ

Is more detailed information about tournaments and teams available?

GRID currently offers all static information available about tournaments and teams through the APIs. We are continuously working towards increasing the level of detail of all available information and will provide incremental updates to extend its support in the future.

Is any information relating to players' rosters/lineups supported?

The APIs currently do not support a team's expected roster / lineup, although this feature is being worked on and will be supported in the future.

n-Game Data Quick-Start Guide

Prerequisites

Before querying for in-game data, you must obtain an API key. You can acquire one from our Support Team. Additionally, you must have access to a tool able to make GraphQL requests, such as the GraphQL Playground or Postman.

Run a query using the GRID Playground

Fill in the API KEY text input with your API key.

Choose the entity you wish to query from the tabs above the editor. LDF Series State is the tab related to the Live Data Feed Series State.

The left panel will show one pre-filled query: GetLiveDotaSeriesState.

To run the query, click the play button at the top of the Playground.

After running the query, the right panel will display the resulting data in JSON format.

Understand the results

The output of the GetLiveDotaSeriesState query provides the live data for a series, the DotA Loopfeed series in this case (a demo DotA series running cyclically on the GRID Platform). The following key data points are included:

Series: data points for a series. Numerous other entities, such as Teams, Players, and Games are nested within this entity. Some data points provided by the static data API are also included in this entity.

valid: denotes whether the data for this series is accurate, based on GRID's assessment. This implies that no issues have been reported to the team.

updatedAt: indicates the time of the last update to this series.

format: specifies how many games are included in the series and how the winner will be determined. In this example, the series is a "best of three" (Bo3), which means up to three games will be played.

started: indicates whether the series has begun.

finished: indicates whether the series has concluded.

teams: provides the name of each team participating in the Series and information regarding whether they have won the series. It is important to note that this data point is on a "series level," implying that it is unrelated to the outcome of individual games. Data points are aggregated on a series level.

games: provides all supported data points for a game.

sequenceNumber: indicates the order in which games have been played.

teams: provides the teams' data points aggregated on a game level.

name: indicates the name of the team.

players: provides the data points for players aggregated on a game level.

kills: indicates the amount of kills a player got in the game.

deaths: indicates how many times the player died in a game.

netWorth: indicates the sum of the player’s inventory value and their current money.

money: indicates the total amount of money the player possesses.

position: the X/Y coordinates of where the player is standing on the map.

Additional Resources

The example includes only some of the GRID Live Data Feed's data points. Please refer to the GraphQL API Schema documentation for a comprehensive list of the available data points. The Schema documentation can be accessed by clicking the Docs button in the GraphQL Playground.

In-Game Data Overview

The GRID data platform enables you to get in-game data via its APIs. By definition this is all data generated by the title’s game server, either

Directly, like a team planting the Spike in Valorant or slaying Roshan in DotA

Indirectly, like a team winning a series after winning 2 games in a Best-of-3 format

The in-game data’s scope is a series, meaning that any in-game data is tracked across one series and not multiple. In-game data refers back to static data, which can be used to tie data for entities across multiple series together.

In-game data includes both

The latest state of a series

Events that happened throughout a series

GRID’s data structure is title-agnostic, meaning that it is the same across all supported titles. This does not mean that all state data points and events are applicable to all titles; only that when they are applicable, they work in exactly the same way.

Series State

The state of a series gives you a snapshot of the latest situation. This state changes over time while the series is ongoing.

Examples of state are

The total kills of a player throughout a series

Whether or not a team has won a game already

A player’s current money and inventory

Series State URLs

There are two URLs that can be used to access the Series State API. One is for Open Access users and the other is for clients with commercial level access.

Open Access URL

https://api-op.grid.gg/live-data-feed/series-state/graphql

Full Access URL

https://api.grid.gg/live-data-feed/series-state/graphql

Data structure

The state of a series follows a hierarchy containing different state levels:

Series

Games

Segments

Segments

…

Each series consists of games being played. Each game can consist of multiple segments being played. Each segment can consist of multiple segments being played and so on. A segment can thus represent

A part of a game, like a round in Valorant

A part of another segment, like the Buy Phase of that round

The state is structured in such a way that the same data points are aggregated on all state levels, for example the total kills throughout the whole series, a single game or a segment of a game. Some data can not be aggregated and only appears on specific state levels, like whether or not a segment is finished yet.

Additionally, state data points are also aggregated per individual participant of a series, like the total kills of a team in a game. These aggregates are available on each state level and follow the following hierarchy:

Teams

Players

Each team’s data points also hold the data points for the players playing for that team.

Getting the latest state

Using our Series State API it is possible to get the latest state of a series. In the request you can ask for exactly the state data points you’re interested in. That way the responses are as quick and minimal as possible.

The state updates as actions happen during an ongoing series. By default, the state will be synchronized with the official broadcast stream.

Currently we don’t offer a way to listen for state changes. If you want to keep knowing about the latest state of an ongoing series, you’ll have to request it again every so often depending on your use case and up to a limit. If you request the state too often and break that limit you’ll get a response telling you to back off from sending more requests for some time.

The state at the end of the series remains accessible after the series is finished. This enables you to request data for past series as well. You can also download the full state for a past series as a file using our File Download API.

You can use our GraphQL Playground to try getting the latest state of a series yourself without having to write any code. We continuously replay test series so you can try it out even when there’s no esports series ongoing.

Series Events

The Series Events API provides real-time, structured updates for ongoing esports series across major titles like CS2, DOTA 2, League of Legends, VALORANT, PUBG, and Rainbow Six Siege. Delivered as JSON transactions over WebSocket, each update contains both the events that occurred and the resulting full or partial state of the series, games, teams, and players.

This API is not included in the Open Access program

What can the Series Events API be used for?

The API enables clients to:

Track Live Progress: Instantly follow match flow, including starts/ends, objectives, kills, and more.

Access State* Snapshots: On connection or via configuration, receive a complete state snapshot to sync or reconstruct the current match at any time.

Filter and Customize Data: Use configuration payloads to filter for specific events or request full state inclusion for selected events.

Handle Game Restorations: On connection or via configuration, receive a complete state snapshot to sync or reconstruct the current match at any time.

Integrate with Reference Data: Combine live state with static data** from the Central Data API for richer applications.

*State is the current situation of the series including data like game number, score, kills, networth etc.

**Static data in this context is data that doesn’t change often such as fixtures, team/player/tournament information etc.

Example Use Cases

Live Broadcasts & Visualization: Power real-time overlays, scoreboards, and in-game stats for esports productions.

Analytics & Insights: Feed data into analytics tools for player performance, economy, and event timelines.

Betting & Integrity: Provide up-to-date, accurate data for betting platforms and integrity monitoring.

Coaching & Review: Enable coaches and analysts to reconstruct matches for review or highlight generation.

Fan Engagement: Drive interactive apps, fantasy games, and notifications based on real-time game events.

Key Features

Hierarchical State Model: Series → Games → Segments → Teams → Players.

Event-Driven & Stateful: Each event carries both its delta* and the resulting state.

Configurable Streams: Filter and tailor the feed to your needs.

Robust Restoration Support: Built-in workflows for re-connection situations.

Cross-Title Consistency: Unified schema with title-specific extensions.

*Delta state is the change from the last known state. For example if a kill happens in a series the kills delta in the message is going to be 1.

Connecting to the API

WebSocket Endpoints

By Series ID:

wss://api.grid.gg/live-data-feed/series/{SERIES_ID}?key={AUTH_KEY}

Available up to 2 hours after the series ends.

By Player ID:

wss://api.grid.gg/live-data-feed/series?playerId={PLAYER_ID}&key={AUTH_KEY}

Remains open and switches to the next series when the player participates again.

Parameters

Parameter

Type

Description

series_id* / playerId*

String

Series or player identifier

key*

String

Authentication key

useConfig

Boolean

If true, expects a configuration payload after connecting

fromSequenceNumber

Int

Start from this transaction number

fromSessionSequenceNumber

Int

Start from this session sequence number

* required parameter

Connection Limits

Max 3 concurrent connections per series per key

Max 5 connection requests per minute per key

Configuration

The API supports runtime filtering and customization of event streams via a configuration payload. This allows clients to:

Exclude or include specific event types

Request full state inclusion on specific events

Configuration Payload Example:

{

  "rules": [

    {

      "eventTypeMatcher": {

        "actor": "",

        "action": "",

        "target": "item"

      },

      "exclude": true,

      "includeFullState": false

    },

    {

      "eventTypeMatcher": {

        "actor": "",

        "action": "killed",

        "target": ""

      },

      "exclude": false,

      "includeFullState": true

    }

  ]

}

eventTypeMatcher: Use empty strings or wildcards (*) for broad matching.

exclude: If true, matched events are excluded from the feed.

includeFullState: If true, the full series/game state is included in the event payload.

How to Apply

Connect with useConfig=true in the URL.

Send the configuration JSON as a text message over the WebSocket after connecting

Event message example

{

  "id": "event-1",

  "type": "series-started-game",

  "includesFullState": false,

  "actor": {

    "type": "series",

    "id": "series-1",

    "stateDelta": {

      "id": "series-1",

      "games": [

        {

          "id": "game-1",

          "started": true

        }

      ]

    },

    "state": {

      "id": "series-1",

      "games": [

        {

          "id": "game-1",

          "started": true

        }

      ]

    }

  },

  "action": "started",

  "target": {

    "type": "game",

    "id": "game-1",

     "stateDelta": {

      "id": "game-1",

      "started": true

    },

    "state": {

      "id": "game-1",

      "started": true

    }

  },

  "seriesStateDelta": {

    "id": "series-1",

    "games": [

      {

        "id": "game-1",

        "started": true

      }

    ]

  },

  "seriesState": {

    "id": "series-1",

    "games": [

      {

        "id": "game-1",

        "started": true

      }

    ]

  }

}

Testing tools

The Series Events API offers a suite of tools and resources to help you test, validate, and integrate your applications before going live with production data. These tools are designed to simulate live series data, provide easy visualization, and allow for robust end-to-end testing.

Feed Viewer

The Feed Viewer is a web-based tool for connecting to any live or test Series Events feed. It allows you to:

Connect using your authentication key and a Series ID or Player ID.

Visualize real-time transactions and events as they are published.

Inspect full state snapshots and event deltas.

Experiment with configuration options and filtering.

![][image1]

How to Access

Visit The Feed Viewer which is publicly accessible. Enter the Series ID (including any Test Loop Series ID) and your authentication key to begin streaming data.

Test Loop Series

GRID provides dedicated Test Loop Series for each supported title. These are continuously running, simulated series that loop through matches for testing purposes. By connecting to a Test Loop Series, you can:

Receive a constant stream of realistic, title-specific events and state changes.

Test your integration, parsing, and visualization logic in a safe environment.

Validate your application's handling of all event types.

Title

Series ID

CS2

28

DOTA 2

2

League of Legends

3

MLBB

11

PUBG

4

Rainbow Six Siege

25

Standoff 2

32

VALORANT

The Test Loop Series ID correlates directly to the Title ID for each game title. Use these IDs in your connection URL to access the corresponding test feed for that title.

GRID File Download API

Overview

The File Download API allows the download of comprehensive gameplay data in file format. This REST API enables users to verify the availability of files for a specific series and obtain the corresponding download links.

For series of the supported titles, users can download the GRID State and Events data files. Additionally, for selected titles, users can download official files provided by game developers, such as Riot Game Agnostic Match History and LiveStats files.

The API is available through the following URL:

https://api.grid.gg/file-download

Specifications

A comprehensive OpenAPI specification is available on the GRID CDN.

File types

This section provides an overview of each available file type, along with a description of its content.

GRID State

As a convenience, the GRID state available on the Series State API can also be downloaded as a file in uncompressed JSON format.

Please refer to the Series State API data structure section for detailed information on the file's content.

Note that while obtaining the full GRID State as a file is helpful for a quick start, it is recommended to use the Series State API directly for a more straightforward understanding of the data structure outlined in its schema. Similar to other GRID GraphQL APIs, the Series State API provides schema documentation and allows the selection of specific data points.

GRID Events

This file type is available in compressed JSONL (as in JSON Lines) format.

The file is composed of transactions, each holding one or more events that occurred at the same time. Each event includes the actor who has caused the event, the action taken and the target of the event. It also includes how the event has changed the GRID state.

Quick-start guide

Prerequisites

To access the File download API, the following prerequisites are required:

The GRID API access key. The same API access key can be used across all GRID APIs. If not yet available, an access key can be requested by contacting Support Team,

a tool capable of executing HTTP GET requests, such as curl, Postman, Insomnia

Steps

Obtain the series ID for which files would be downloaded. The series IDs are shown in the Match History Viewer or can be retrieved from the Central Data Feed.

Get available files for a series by executing an HTTP GET request, including your key, as described in the Authentication section of the document. For example, when querying for series ID 2537521 with the API key being personal-api-key, the request using curl would be the following:

curl -i -H "x-api-key: personal-api-key" https://api.grid.gg/file-download/list/2537521

Request

https://api.grid.gg/file-download/list/{seriesId}

Header

Description

x-api-key

Your personal API Key

Response

{

    "files": [

        {

            "id": "events-riot-compressed",

            "description": "Riot LiveStats (.zip)",

            "status": "ready",

            "fileName": "events_2537521_riot.jsonl.zip",

            "fullURL": "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/events/riot/series/2537521"

        },

        {

            "id": "state-riot-compressed",

            "description": "Riot Game Agnostic Match History (.zip)",

            "status": "ready",

            "fileName": "end_state_2537521_riot.json.zip",

            "fullURL": "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/riot/series/2537521"

        },

        {

            "id": "events-grid-compressed",

            "description": "Grid Series Events (.zip)",

            "status": "ready",

            "fileName": "events_2537521_grid.jsonl.zip",

            "fullURL": "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/events/grid/series/2537521"

        },

        {

            "id": "state-grid",

            "description": "Grid Post Series State (.json)",

            "status": "ready",

            "fileName": "end_state_2537521_grid.json",

            "fullURL": "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2537521"

        }

    ]

}

If the status of a file type is "ready", it can be downloaded by executing another HTTP GET request using the fullURL value from the response of the list request.

Stats Feed Overview

The GRID Stats Feed comprises a set of APIs that present the aggregated values of in-game data in order to produce customizable statistics and analytics.

The GRID Stats Feed leverages the quality of official data and the game-title-agnostic capabilities of the GRID Data Platform to create a comprehensive, easily accessible suite of statistics, which enables users to create bespoke insights for their audiences.

The GRID Stats Feed offers aggregated statistics for teams and players for a given series or game sample. For example, the win rate over the last three months, the minimum/maximum/average kills in a tournament, or the number of structures destroyed per match in the last year.

Access

The Stats Feed API is a GraphQL API that can be accessed using the following endpoint:

https://api-op.grid.gg/statistics-feed/graphql

In order to make requests, authentication using an API key is required. This key can be added to the request by setting the following header.

x-api-key=<valid-api-key>

For a list of GraphQL tools available for a multitude of different languages, see here.

Please note: the tools linked above are not maintained or supported by GRID esports and license information for each should be understood and adhered to.

Filters

The Stats Feed allows the definition of series or game samples with different conditions. For example, by tournament or time window.

Name

Type

Description

tournamentIds

IdFilter

Allows filtering by up to 20 Tournament IDs.

timeWindow

TimeRangeFilter

Allows filtering by a set time frame.

Other sampling conditions are supported depending on the query. See the API Reference for further details.

Limitations

The following limitations have to be considered when using the filters:

The tournamentIds and timeWindows filters are mutually exclusive; using both will return a BAD_REQUEST error.

Only users with access to all series of a title can use the timeWindow filter.

Users with tournament-specific permissions are required to use the tournamentIds filter.

Statistics Structure

The Stats Feed follows a very similar structure to GRID Series State API, where Segments (rounds) are nested inside Games, which in turn are nested inside Series (matches).

The following high-level stats are currently supported; refer to the API Reference for detailed information.

Term

Description

Notes

teamStatistics

Analyses the performance of a specified team in a series sample. Data points are aggregated by the team ID and by series, games, and segment.

For example, sum/min/max/avg kills of the series played in the last three months for team with ID=1234

teamGameStatistics

Analyses the performance of a specified team in a game sample. Data points are aggregated by the team ID and by games and segment.

For example, sum/min/max/avg kills of the games played on a specific map during a tournament for the team with ID=1234

playerStatistics

Analyses the performance of a specified player in a series sample. Data points are aggregated by the player ID and by series, games, and segments.

For example, sum/min/max/avg kills of the series played in the last year for the player with ID=1234

Example

Query the sum, minimum, maximum, and average of the kills, deaths, and net worth the CSGO team with id 45021 scored in the last six months. Also, query the win rate and the shortest, longest, and current win streak.

Try it out

query {

  teamStatistics(teamId: "45021", filter: { timeWindow: LAST_6_MONTHS }) {

    series {

      count

      kills {

        sum

        min

        max

        avg

      }

      deaths {

        sum

        min

        max

        avg

      }

    }

    game {

      count

      netWorth {

        sum

        min

        max

        avg

      }

      wins {

        value

        count

        percentage

        streak {

          min

          max

          current

        }

      }

    }

    segment {

      type

      count

      kills {

        sum

        min

        max

        avg

      }

      wins {

        value

        count

        percentage

        streak {

          min

          max

          current

        }

      }

    }

  }

}

The JSON response may be similar to the following

{

  "data": {

    "teamStatistics": {

      "series": {

        "count": 41,

        "kills": {

          "sum": 8943,

          "min": 133,

          "max": 334,

          "avg": 218.1219512195122

        },

        "deaths": {

          "sum": 8912,

          "min": 135,

          "max": 334,

          "avg": 217.3658536585366

        }

      },

      "game": {

        "count": 95,

        "netWorth": {

          "sum": 1902300,

          "min": 1550,

          "max": 78350,

          "avg": 20024.21052631579

        },

        "wins": [

          {

            "value": false,

            "count": 47,

            "percentage": 49.473684210526315,

            "streak": {

              "min": 1,

              "max": 9,

              "current": 0

            }

          },

          {

            "value": true,

            "count": 48,

            "percentage": 50.526315789473685,

            "streak": {

              "min": 1,

              "max": 11,

              "current": 1

            }

          }

        ]

      },

      "segment": [

        {

          "type": "round",

          "count": 2519,

          "kills": {

            "sum": 8943,

            "min": 0,

            "max": 5,

            "avg": 3.550218340611354

          },

          "wins": [

            {

              "value": false,

              "count": 1243,

}

Supported Titles

The Stats Feed API follows GRID’s title-agnostic design principle and is available for all GRID-supported titles, including League of Legends, Counter Strike 2, Defense of the Ancients 2, Valorant, PUBG, Rainbow Six: Siege*.

*Title support may be limited to specific statistics. See the Statistics Structure section for details.

Supported Statistics

Some of the statistics the GRID Stats API supports are: count (of series, games, rounds), kills, killAssistsGiven, killAssistsReceived, teamkills, teamkillAssistsGiven, teamkillAssistsReceived, selfkills, deaths, headshots, structuresDestroyed, structuresCaptured, score and wins.

See the API reference for a comprehensive list of the supported statistics and their description.

Statistics types

Statistics can be of different types depending on their purpose.

Int

This type of statistic is a single aggregated integer.

Example

Total number of Series for the applied filter (count):

{

  "data": {

    "teamStatistics": {

      "series": {

        "count": 244

      }

    }

  }

}

The above response shows that 244 Series were included in this range (title ID, team ID & time window).

AggregateIntStatistic

This type of statistic is an aggregation of integer fields, which includes the total (sum), the minimum (min), the maximum (max) and the average (avg). Some of the statistics using this type are kills, killAssistsGiven, killAssistsReceived, teamkills, teamkillAssistsGiven, teamkillAssistsReceived, selfkills, deaths, headshots, structuresDestroyed, structuresCaptured and score.

Example

Sum, min, max and avg values of kills (Series level) and netWorth (Game level) Total number of Series in range (count) for the applied filter:

{

  "data": {

    "teamStatistics": {

      "series": {

        "kills": {

          "sum": 55807,

          "min": 90,

          "max": 459,

          "avg": 228.7172131147541

        }

      },

      "game": {

        "count": 598,

        "netWorth": {

          "sum": 11342450,

          "min": 1100,

          "max": 80800,

          "avg": 18967.30769230769

        }

      }

    }

  }

}

The above response shows that the team had a total of 55807 kills, with minimum, maximum and average values of 90, 459 and 228.71, respectively per Series. The net worth of all the players across all games was 11342450 with a minimum, maximum and average value of 1100, 80800 and 18967.3 per Game, respectively.

BooleanOccurenceStatistic

This type of statistic counts the total number (count) of occurrences for a certain boolean condition (Boolean), such as, for example, a Team having won a Game. Additional statistics are also provided, such as the percentage value as well as the following streak-related statistics: min, max and current.

Example

Game win statistics for the applied filter:

{

  "data": {

    "teamStatistics": {

      "game": {

        "wins": [

          {

            "value": false,

            "count": 320,

            "percentage": 53.333333333333336,

            "streak": {

              "min": 1,

              "max": 14,

              "current": 4

            }

          },

          {

            "value": true,

            "count": 280,

            "percentage": 46.666666666666664,

            "streak": {

              "min": 1,

              "max": 10,

              "current": 0

            }

          }

        ]

      }

    }

  }

}

The above response shows that the team lost 320 Games, corresponding to 53.33% of the total Games played in the period. The shortest losing streak was 1 Game, while the longest was 14. They are currently on a 4 game losing streak. Respectively, the statistics for games won are 280 total, a 46.66% win rate, a shortest winning streak of 1, a longest winning streak of 10 and a current winning streak of 0.

Post-Game Data API Overview 

This document outlines the process for transmitting post-game data to the GRID Data Platform, making it accessible via the GRID Post-Game API. It details the key integration steps, including sending commands that represent in-game actions (like kills or item pickups) and updating the overall game state.

Key aspects of the integration include:

Commands: Data is transmitted as JSON commands via HTTPS to the GRID Telemetry API.

Game State Updates: The UPDATE_BASIC_GAME_STATE command provides an overview of the game's final state.

Actions: Individual actions within the game can be tracked using specific commands (e.g., KILL_ENEMY_PLAYER).

Player Positions: The UPDATE_PLAYER_POSITIONS command allows for tracking player coordinates over time.

Correlation ID: This ID allows associating actions, position updates, and state changes for synchronized processing.

API Key: Provided by GRID, along with title IDs for production and testing.

OpenAPI Specification: The grid_openapi_post_game_api.yaml file is provided to define the API structure, viewable in the Swagger Editor. Link to Download

A game integration process generally involves a collaborative effort with GRID's Solutions Architects, who assist in designing, implementing, testing, and monitoring the integration.

It's imporant to note that not all data is required to be transmitted and data entities (teams, players, etc.) can be dynamically created or pre-created.

If there are any questions, always feel free to reach out to support@grid.gg.

Post-Game Data API Quick-Start Guide

This guide will get you up and running with the basics of transmitting post-game data to the GRID Data Platform.

1. Prerequisites:

API key, 'title id' (for production), and 'test title id' (for development) from GRID.

grid_openapi_post_game_api.yaml file (OpenAPI specification). Link to Download

A game server or system capable of sending HTTPS requests.

Familiarity with JSON data format.

2. Set up your environment:

Use the provided API keys and title IDs. Keep the production and test credentials separate.

Open the grid_openapi_post_game_api.yaml file in the Swagger Editor to explore the API structure and available commands.

3. Transmit basic game state:

After a game ends, send an UPDATE_BASIC_GAME_STATE command via HTTP.

Include a unique game ID in the request.

This single command is enough to make game statistics available through the GRID Post-Game GraphQL API.

Example (Conceptual JSON):

{

  "command": "UPDATE_BASIC_GAME_STATE",

  "game_id": "your_unique_game_id",

  "game_result": "win",

  "player_count": 10

  //... other relevant game state data

}

4. Enhance with Actions:

For each significant in-game action (e.g., kill, item pickup), transmit the corresponding command (e.g., KILL_ENEMY_PLAYER).

The OpenAPI specification details available commands and required fields.

Example (Conceptual JSON):

{

    "command": "KILL_ENEMY_PLAYER",

    "killer_id": "player123",

    "victim_id": "player456",

    "game_id": "your_unique_game_id"

}

5. Track Player Positions:

Use the UPDATE_PLAYER_POSITIONS command to send player coordinates.

Include this command whenever an action occurs. Use a "correlation id" to link actions and positions.

Send UPDATE_PLAYER_POSITIONS at regular intervals (e.g., once per second) for continuous tracking.

Example (Conceptual JSON):

{

    "command": "UPDATE_PLAYER_POSITIONS",

    "correlation_id": "unique_action_id",

    "positions": [

        {

            "player_id": "player123",

            "x": 10.5,

            "y": 20.2,

            "z": 5.0

        }

      // ... more player positions

    ]

}

6. Advanced State Changes:

Send UPDATE_BASIC_GAME_STATE commands periodically to reflect ongoing changes in the game.

Correlate these updates with actions or positions using the same "correlation id" if necessary.

7. Verification:

After sending data, verify that it's available via the GRID Post-Game GraphQL API using the game ID.

Key Considerations:

Work with GRID's integration specialists to design a tailored plan.

Transmit only the data relevant to your game.

Use your own IDs for data entities (players, teams, etc.).

GRID provides support for managing data entity mappings.

Choose a transmission strategy (single batch or real-time) that suits your game server's architecture.

This guide provides a high-level overview. Please refer to the full documentation and OpenAPI specification for detailed information on all available commands and parameters.

Post-Game Visualisations Overview

Product Walkthrough: Analyzing Post Game Data

1. Navigating to Post Game Data

Start on the Game Selection Page: You'll begin on the main screen where you can see a list of your games.

Filters: Use the "Filters" section to narrow down your game selection. You can filter by "GAME TITLE" or "PLAYERS".

Game Details: On the Game Selection Page, you'll see a list of individual matches or sessions played. You can from this view see overview information, such as a Game/Session ID, Game Duration, Map Played and Game Score.

Choose a Match: Click on the game or session you want to analyze further. This will take you to the "Post Game Data" page. You also have the option to download the game file directly from here.

2. Exploring the Post Game Data Page

Statistics Table Section:

In this view you have a detailed overview of the stats from the game.

In the tabbed interface, you can toggle between "Player" and "Team" views to analyze individual or collective stats.

In the Statistic Table itself, you will find:

Rows representing Player/Team Names.

Columns representing e.g., Kills scores, Assists, etc.). Note that you can hover the column title to get the unabbreviated version.

Comparison Table Section:

This view looks at team performance and compares it against each other. These comparisons can also be implemented as a radar/spider views

If there are any questions, always feel free to reach out to support@grid.gg.

Overview

The GRID APIs are a mixture of REST, GraphQL and WebSocket based APIs.

Within this reference area you'll find individual documentation for each API we offer to you along with which protocol to use for this API.

Feed Overview

Central Data Feed

Query API: a GraphQL API exposing information about titles, tournaments, teams and series (scheduling).

Live Data Feed

Series State API: a GraphQL API exposing the current state of a live series (updated as actions happen during an ongoing game) and the final state of previously played series.

Series Events API: a Websocket API that enables clients to listen for events that are pushed to them as they occur during a live series.

File Download API: a REST API that allows the download of the complete gameplay data of a previously played series.

Access

Access to the GRID APIs is different for every consumer, which can vary on both per API and also for the title, tournament and individual series being accessed.

Bulk Access

Bulk requests are not supported, so instead a single request for every object is required.

Authentication

GRID's APIs use API Keys to authenticate requests, you can manage API Keys by contacting our support team.

These API Keys carry a lot of privilege so try ensure you keep these secret and secure. Don't share these with others, or upload to public spaces such as GitHub.

GRID's APIs utilise two different protocols HTTP and WebSocket, due to limitations our WebSocket API's

REST/GraphQL

As both of these standards utilise HTTP underneath we can use the x-api-key header with the value being that of our API Key provided to you.

var headers = {

	'x-api-key': 'XXX'

}

WebSocket

To access our WebSocket based connections you will need to use a QueryParam appended to the end of the wss url you are using to connect to the API.

wss://api.grid.gg...?key=XXX

All of our requests must be used using SSL therefor please ensure your using HTTPS or WSS endpoints when querying for data.

GraphQL

Authentication

Users of all the GRID APIs must identify themselves before consuming the APIs. The authentication process requires passing a key to the API.

When consuming a GraphQL API, the API key can be passed by setting the x-api-key header in the HTTP request. The way in which this is achieved will vary depending on the specific tool being utilized.

More information about the GraphQL authorization mechanism can be found in the official documentation located at this page.

Pagination

GRID APIs can be used to retrieve all the series for a given time period. While querying for short time periods may yield a small list of series in the response, querying for larger periods, such as a year, would result in larger lists of series. In this latter case, pagination is used to split the results into multiple pages.

GRID APIs maximum page length is 50 results. Thus, a single query will return no more than 50 series. The caller can adjust the page length, and it is currently set to 10 results by default.

Let us consider the following query, which can be found in the GRID Playground. The query requests all the series that started between 03/11/2021 and 04/11/2021, and it will yield the first 10 series from that period.

query GetAllSeriesInNext24Hours {

  allSeries(

    filter:{

      startTimeScheduled:{

        gte: "2021-11-03T00:00:00+01:00"

        lte: "2021-11-04T00:00:00+01:00"

      }

    }

    orderBy: StartTimeScheduled

  ) {

    totalCount,

    pageInfo{

      hasPreviousPage

      hasNextPage

      startCursor

      endCursor

    }

    edges{

      cursor

      node{

        id

        startTimeScheduled

      }

    }

  }

}

The resulting JSON response can be similar to the following:

{

  "data": {

    "allSeries": {

      "totalCount": 32,

      "pageInfo": {

        "hasPreviousPage": false,

        "hasNextPage": true,

        "startCursor": "JAMWBQMjHhoSJBQfEhMCGxITCwtaCwtERUdORUcLC1oLC0VHRUZaRkZaR0QjR05NR0dNR0ct",

        "endCursor": "JAMWBQMjHhoSJBQfEhMCGxITCwtaCwtERUZHRUULC1oLC0VHRUZaRkZaR0QjRkVNR0dNR0ct"

      },

      "edges": [...]

    }

  }

}

To understand this response, it is necessary to examine the following three fields values:

totalCount refers to the number of results matching the given filter.

hasNextPage indicates whether further querying is required to obtain all the results.

endCursor works like a bookmark. It indicates where further queries should start in order to get the next set of results.

Based on the above information, the following query can be executed in order to obtain the next set of results:

query GetAllSeriesInNext24Hours {

  allSeries(

    after: "JAMWBQMjHhoSJBQfEhMCGxITCwtaCwtERUZHRUULC1oLC0VHRUZaRkZaR0QjRkVNR0dNR0ct"

    filter:{

      startTimeScheduled:{

        gte: "2021-11-03T00:00:00+01:00"

        lte: "2021-11-04T00:00:00+01:00"

      }

    }

    orderBy: StartTimeScheduled

  ) {

    totalCount,

    pageInfo{

      hasPreviousPage

      hasNextPage

      startCursor

      endCursor

    }

    edges{

      cursor

      node{

        id

        startTimeScheduled

      }

    }

  }

}

Notably, the after field is set with the value of the endCursor field from the result of the previous query. This ensures that the first item of the returned result is the one following the last of the first query. In order to fetch the entire result set, it is sufficient to keep executing queries, passing the value of the endCursor of the previous result, until the hasNextPage field is set to false.

Instead, in order to get all the results in one query - but always up to 50 - it would be sufficient to specify the first field in the query:

query GetAllSeriesInNext24Hours {

  allSeries(

    first: 50

    filter:{

      startTimeScheduled:{

        gte: "2021-11-03T09:05:39+01:00"

        lte: "2021-11-04T09:05:39+01:00"

      }

    }

    orderBy: StartTimeScheduled

  ) {

    totalCount,

    pageInfo{

      hasPreviousPage

      hasNextPage

      startCursor

      endCursor

    }

    edges{

      cursor

      node{

        id

        startTimeScheduled

      }

    }

  }

}

The first field indicates the number of items we request. This can be any number, from 1 to 50. The first field has a counterpart: last, which allows querying the results the other way around; instead of returning the first X results that match the given filter, the result will include the last X results.

More information on the GraphQL pagination can be found in the official documentation here.

Rate limit

The rate limit restricts the number of queries a user can execute in a time period.

By default, GRID allows 40 requests per minute for Closed Platform and 20 requests per minute for Open Platform. Any more attempts will be rejected.

Check the right API key is passed. If the API key is correct, users may contact the GRID Support team for assistance.

UNAUTHORIZED

The API key provided has no access to the product/content.

Contact the GRID Support team to get the proper permissions.

        "errorType": "BAD_REQUEST",

        "errorDetail": "INVALID_ARGUMENT",

        "exception": {

          "locations": [],

          "path": [

          ]

        }

      }

    }

  ],

  "data": null

}

WebSocket

WebSocket connections allow for two-way communication. Once a connection is opened, either side can push a message to the other side.

WebSocket connections are used to push data to the client. This enables clients to open a connection to listen for data even before it is available. This article presents details about the behavior of WebSocket connections.

Authentication

To confirm the client's identity, information must be passed on to each of the APIs.

When using WebSockets, the client's personal API key is used for authentication, and this information should be passed as a query parameter 'key' when opening a connection. For example, if the client's personal API key is 'secret-personal-api-key', then the URL to open a connection would be:

wss://api.grid.gg/live-data-feed/series/1?key=secret-personal-api-key

Clients can retrieve their personal API key here.

Limits

WebSockets usage is limited by GRID to ensure the system's proper operation, and these limits are applied per personal API key.

Rate limit

The rate limit restricts the client in terms of how many connection attempts can be made within a certain period.

By default, X connection attempts per minute are allowed. Any additional connection attempts will be rejected.

Connection limit

The connection limit restricts the number of simultaneous connections the client can have open at any given time.

By default, Y connections are allowed to be open at the same time. Any additional connection attempts will be rejected.

Duration limit

The duration limit restricts the duration for which a WebSocket connection can remain open. This limit is reset when a Data or Control frame is sent from either side.

By default, a WebSocket connection can remain open for up to 24 hours after the last activity. After this time, the WebSocket connection is automatically closed.

If clients wish to keep inactive WebSocket connections open for a longer period, they can periodically send WebSocket Ping Control frames.

Mutations

createPlayer

Creates a new GRID player. Returns CreatePlayerPayload!.

Argument

Type

Description

createPlayerInput

CreatePlayerInput!

Expects the nickname, the team the player belongs to and the title the player participates in and optionally the external links associated with the player.

Argument

Type

Description

createPlayerRoleInput

CreatePlayerRoleInput!

Expects the name of the role and title that the role is associated with.

Argument

Type

Description

createSeriesInput

CreateSeriesInput!

Expects the title for the series, the tournament where it's being played, the teams playing it, the start date and time, and the format.

Argument

Type

Description

createTeamInput

CreateTeamInput!

Expects the name, the title the team participates in and optionally the primary and/or secondary colors, the logo of the team and the external links associated with the team.

Argument

Type

Description

createTournamentInput

CreateTournamentInput!

Expects the name and short name, and optionally the titles for the tournament, the teams playing in it, and the logo of the tournament.

ErrorDetail

Field

Description

DEADLINE_EXCEEDED

The deadline expired before the operation could complete. For operations that change the state of the system, this error may be returned even if the operation has completed successfully. For example, a successful response from a server could have been delayed long enough for the deadline to expire. HTTP Mapping: 504 Gateway Timeout Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 420 Enhance Your Calm Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

FIELD_NOT_FOUND

The requested field is not found in the schema. This differs from

INVALID_ARGUMENT

The client specified an invalid argument. Note that this differs from

INVALID_CURSOR

The provided cursor is not valid. The most common usage for this error is when a client is paginating through a list that uses stateful cursors. In that case, the provided cursor may be expired. HTTP Mapping: 404 Not Found Error Type: NOT_FOUND

MISSING_RESOURCE

Unable to perform operation because a required resource is missing. Example: Client is attempting to refresh a list, but the specified list is expired. This requires an action by the client to get a new list. If the user is simply trying GET a resource that is not found, use the NOT_FOUND error type. FAILED_PRECONDITION.MISSING_RESOURCE is to be used particularly when the user is performing an operation that requires a particular resource to exist. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request or 500 Internal Server Error Error Type: FAILED_PRECONDITION

SERVICE_ERROR

Service Error. There is a problem with an upstream service. This may be returned if a gateway receives an unknown error from a service or if a service is unreachable. If a request times out which waiting on a response from a service,

TCP_FAILURE

Request failed due to network errors. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

THROTTLED_CONCURRENCY

Request throttled based on server concurrency limits. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

THROTTLED_CPU

Request throttled based on server CPU limits HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable. Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

TOO_MANY_REQUESTS

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 429 Too Many Requests Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

UNIMPLEMENTED

The operation is not implemented or is not currently supported/enabled. HTTP Mapping: 501 Not Implemented Error Type: BAD_REQUEST

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. This error should only be returned when no other error detail applies. If a client sees an unknown errorDetail, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

ErrorType

Field

Description

BAD_REQUEST

Bad Request. There is a problem with the request. Retrying the same request is not likely to succeed. An example would be a query or argument that cannot be deserialized. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request

FAILED_PRECONDITION

The operation was rejected because the system is not in a state required for the operation's execution. For example, the directory to be deleted is non-empty, an rmdir operation is applied to a non-directory, etc. Service implementers can use the following guidelines to decide between

INTERNAL

Internal error. An unexpected internal error was encountered. This means that some invariants expected by the underlying system have been broken. This error code is reserved for serious errors. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

NOT_FOUND

The requested entity was not found. This could apply to a resource that has never existed (e.g. bad resource id), or a resource that no longer exists (e.g. cache expired.) Note to server developers: if a request is denied for an entire class of users, such as gradual feature rollout or undocumented allowlist,

PERMISSION_DENIED

The caller does not have permission to execute the specified operation.

UNAUTHENTICATED

The request does not have valid authentication credentials. This is intended to be returned only for routes that require authentication. HTTP Mapping: 401 Unauthorized

UNAVAILABLE

Currently Unavailable. The service is currently unavailable. This is most likely a transient condition, which can be corrected by retrying with a backoff. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. For example, this error may be returned when an error code received from another address space belongs to an error space that is not known in this address space. Also errors raised by APIs that do not return enough error information may be converted to this error. If a client sees an unknown errorType, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. Unknown errors MUST NOT trigger any special behavior. These MAY be treated by an implementation as being equivalent to INTERNAL. When possible, a more specific error should be provided. HTTP Mapping: 520 Unknown Error

Scalars

Boolean

The Boolean scalar type represents true or false.

Date

Date formatted as ISO 8601.

DateTime

DateTime formatted as ISO 8601.

Decimal

Decimal number representation.

Float

The Float scalar type represents signed double-precision fractional values as specified by IEEE 754.

HexColor

Hexadecimal value of an RGB color.

ID

The ID scalar type represents a unique identifier, often used to refetch an object or as key for a cache. The ID type appears in a JSON response as a String; however, it is not intended to be human-readable. When expected as an input type, any string (such as "4") or integer (such as 4) input value will be accepted as an ID.

Int

The Int scalar type represents non-fractional signed whole numeric values. Int can represent values between -(2^31) and 2^31 - 1.

String

The String scalar type represents textual data, represented as UTF-8 character sequences. The String type is most often used by GraphQL to represent free-form human-readable text.

Url

URL pointing to resource.

GRID ID of this Player.

name

String!

Name of this Player.

character

Character

In-game character (ie champion, class) of the Player in this Game

roles

[PlayerRole!]!

Roles this Player has in this Game.(available from version "3.43")

participationStatus

ParticipationStatus!

Indicates the participation status of a player for this Game

money

Int!

Amount of money this Player is holding in cash.Depending on the Title this may represent in-game gold, credits, gems etc.

loadoutValue

Int!

Total value (worth in money) of this Player’s loadout.

netWorth

Int!

Sum of money and inventoryValue for this Player.

kills

Int!

Number of enemy kills for this Player in this Game.

killAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists received by this Player in this Game.

killAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists provided by this Player in this Game.

killAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[KillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of enemy KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on kill assists received by this Player in this Game.

weaponKills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of enemy kills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Player in this Game.

teamkills

Int!

Number of teamkills for this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of teamkill assists received by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of teamkill assists provided by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member

teamkillAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[TeamkillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on teamkill assists received by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

weaponTeamkills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of teamkills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

selfkills

Int!

Number of selfkills (suicides) for this Player in this Game.

deaths

Int!

Number of deaths for this Player in this Game.

firstKill

Boolean!

Indication of player acquiring first kill.(available from version "3.10")

Int!

Number of structures destroyed by this Player in this Game.

Float!

The ratio of kills and assists given vs deaths.(available from version "3.27")

Float!

The percentage of this player's kills and assists compared to the overall team's kills.(available from version "3.35")

Float!

The sum of kills and assists given.(available from version "3.34")

maxHealth

Int!

The max amount of health of the player.

Float!

Float!

The amount of money earned per minute.(available from version "3.36")

ClockState!

Respawn clock state to indicate when this player respawns.(available from version "3.3")

Int!

The total amount of money that was earned by this player.(available from version "3.2")

visionScore

Float!

Indicates how much vision this player has influenced in the game, including the vision that was granted and denied.(available from version "3.30")

visionScorePerMinute

Float!

The vision score gained per minute.(available from version "3.33")

Field

Type

Description

id

ID!

GRID ID of this Player.

name

String!

Name of this Player.

character

Character

In-game character (ie champion, class) of the Player in this Game

roles

[PlayerRole!]!

Roles this Player has in this Game.(available from version "3.43")

participationStatus

ParticipationStatus!

Indicates the participation status of a player for this Game

money

Int!

Amount of money this Player is holding in cash.Depending on the Title this may represent in-game gold, credits, gems etc.

loadoutValue

Int!

Total value (worth in money) of this Player’s loadout.

netWorth

Int!

Sum of money and inventoryValue for this Player.

kills

Int!

Number of enemy kills for this Player in this Game.

killAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists received by this Player in this Game.

killAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists provided by this Player in this Game.

killAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[KillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of enemy KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on kill assists received by this Player in this Game.

weaponKills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of enemy kills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Player in this Game.

headshots

Int!

Number of enemy headshots for this Player.(available until version "1.9")

teamkills

Int!

Number of teamkills for this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of teamkill assists received by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of teamkill assists provided by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member

teamkillAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[TeamkillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on teamkill assists received by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

weaponTeamkills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of teamkills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Player in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamHeadshots

Int!

Number of allied headshots for this Player.(available until version "1.9")

selfkills

Int!

Number of selfkills (suicides) for this Player in this Game.

deaths

Int!

Number of deaths for this Player in this Game.

firstKill

Boolean!

Indication of player acquiring first kill.(available from version "3.10")

structuresDestroyed

Int!

Number of structures destroyed by this Player in this Game.

structuresCaptured

Int!

Number of structures captured by this Player in this Game.

inventory

PlayerInventory!

The Player's inventory

objectives

[Objective!]!

A list of objectives that were fulfilled by this Player in this Game.

position

Coordinates

Player Coordinates on the map

multikills

[Multikill!]!

A list of multi kills that happened by this Player in this Game.(available from version "1.7")

unitKills

[UnitKill!]!

A list of unit kills that happened by this Player in this Game.(available from version "3.1")

abilities

[DefaultAbility!]!

A list of abilities that are owned by this Player in this Game.(available from version "1.8")

statusEffects

[StatusEffect!]!

A list of status effects affecting the player(available from version "3.31")

alive

Boolean!

Indicates whether the player is alive.

currentHealth

Int!

The current health of the player.

damageDealt

Int!

The amount of damage dealt.

damageTaken

Int!

The amount of total damage taken.

maxHealth

Int!

The max amount of health of the player.

selfdamageDealt

Int!

The amount of damage dealt to self.

selfdamageTaken

Int!

The amount of damage taken from self.

teamdamageDealt

Int!

The amount of damage dealt to team.

teamdamageTaken

Int!

The amount of damage taken from team.

healingDealt

Int!

The amount of healing dealt by team.(available from version "3.5")

healingReceived

Int!

The amount of healing received by team.(available from version "3.5")

knockdownsGiven

Int!

Number of times of knocking down an enemy for this player.(available from version "3.9")

knockdownsReceived

Int!

Number of times of being knocked down for this player.(available from version "3.9")

damageDealtSources

[DamageDealtSource!]!

A list of damage sources.(available from version "3.17")

damageDealtTargets

[DamageDealtTarget!]!

A list of damage targets.(available from version "3.17")

GameState

Data points for a Game.

Field

Type

Description

id

ID!

GRID ID of this Game.

sequenceNumber

Int!

SequenceNumber of the Game state update.

map

MapState!

Information on the map of this Game.

titleVersion

TitleVersion

Indicates the game version(available from version "3.12")

type

GameType

Indicates the game type(available from version "3.21")

started

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Game has started.

finished

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Game has finished.

forfeited

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Game was forfeited.(available from version "3.48")

paused

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Game is paused.

startedAt

DateTime

DateTime value when this Game was started.(available from version "3.7")

clock

ClockState

Clock state to indicate time of the game(available from version "1.3")

structures

[StructureState!]!

A list of StructureState, containing information about the structures that are available in this Game.

nonPlayerCharacters

[NonPlayerCharacterState!]!

A list of NonPlayerCharacterState, containing information about the state of NPCs in this Game.

teams

[GameTeamState!]!

A list of GameTeamState, containing information on the teams participating in this Game.

draftActions

[DraftAction!]!

A list of DraftAction, containing information about draft actions in this Game.

externalLinks

[ExternalLink!]!

A list of ExternalLink, containing information about links to externally provided IDs.(available from version "1.2")

segments

[SegmentState!]!

A list of SegmentStates, containing information of the segments in this Game.(available from version "1.4")

duration

Duration!

Duration of the Game.(available from version "3.15")

GameTeamStateCs2

CS2 data points for a Team, aggregated for a Game.

Field

Type

Description

id

ID!

GRID ID of this Team.

name

String!

Name of this Team.

side

String!

Side that this Team has taken in this Game ie Red or Blue, Terrorists or Counter-Terrorists.

won

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Team has won this Game.

score

Int!

Score for this Team in this Game. This is used in the Score After format.

money

Int!

Amount of money this Team is holding in cash.Depending on the Title this may represent in-game gold, credits, gems etc.

loadoutValue

Int!

Total value (worth in money) of all the loadouts owned by Players that are members of this Team.

netWorth

Int!

Sum of money and inventoryValue for this Team.

kills

Int!

Number of enemy kills for this Team in this Game.

killAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists received by this Team in this Game.

killAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of enemy kill assists provided by this Team in this Game.

killAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[KillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of enemy KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on kill assists from a Player, received by this Team in this Game.

weaponKills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of enemy kills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Team in this Game.

teamkills

Int!

Number of teamkills for this Team in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsReceived

Int!

Number of teamkill assists received by this Team in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsGiven

Int!

Number of teamkill assists provided by this Team in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

teamkillAssistsReceivedFromPlayer

[TeamkillAssistFromPlayer!]!

A list of KillAssistFromPlayer, containing information on teamkill assists from a Player, received by this Team in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

weaponTeamkills

[WeaponKill!]!

A list of teamkills, which were executed with a specific weapon by this Team in this Game.A teamkill is the occurrence of killing an allied member.

selfkills

Int!

Number of selfkills (suicides) for this Team in this Game.

deaths

Int!

Number of deaths for this Team in this Game.

firstKill

Boolean!

Indication of team acquiring first kill.(available from version "3.10")

structuresDestroyed

Int!

Number of structures destroyed by this Team in this Game.

structuresCaptured

Int!

Number of structures captured by this Team in this Game.

objectives

[Objective!]!

A list of objectives that were fulfilled by this Team in this Game.

unitKills

[UnitKill!]!

A list of unit kills that happened by this Team in this Game.(available from version "3.1")

players

[GamePlayerState!]!

A list of GamePlayerState, containing information about the Players that are members of this Team.

multikills

[Multikill!]!

A list of multi kills that happened by this Team in this Game.(available from version "1.7")

damageDealt

Int!

The amount of damage dealt.

damageTaken

Int!

The amount of total damage taken.

Int!

Int!

The amount of experience points gathered by this team.

Float!

The average percentage of game time each player of this team spent on the opponent's side of the map.(available from version "3.42")

Float!

The ratio of kills and assists given vs deaths.(available from version "3.27")

Float!

The sum of kills and assists given.(available from version "3.34")

majorMoneyDeficit

Float!

The percentage of game time this team owned 48.5% or less of the overall game's gold up to the 40th minute.(available from version "3.41")

majorMoneyLead

Float!

The percentage of game time this team owned 51.5% or more of the overall game's gold up to the 40th minute.(available from version "3.40")

Int!

The total money earned difference to the opponent team.(available from version "3.28")

Float!

The amount of money earned per minute.(available from version "3.36")

Int!

The total amount of money that was earned by this team.(available from version "3.2")

Float!

Indicates how much vision this team has influenced in the game, including the vision it granted and denied.(available from version "3.30")

Float!

The vision score gained per minute.(available from version "3.33")

Description

Title!

String!

Format of this Series e.g. Best of 3 (Bo3).

started

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Series has started.

finished

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Series has finished.

forfeited

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Series was forfeited.(available from version "3.48")

Boolean!

Indicates whether this Series data is considered accurate.

A list of SeriesTeamState, containing information about the Teams participating in this Series.

[GameState!]!

A list of GameState, containing information about the Games in this Series

DateTime!

DateTime
