Enums

ErrorDetail

Field

Description

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. This error should only be returned when no other error detail applies. If a client sees an unknown errorDetail, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

FIELD_NOT_FOUND

The requested field is not found in the schema. This differs from

INVALID_CURSOR

The provided cursor is not valid. The most common usage for this error is when a client is paginating through a list that uses stateful cursors. In that case, the provided cursor may be expired. HTTP Mapping: 404 Not Found Error Type: NOT_FOUND

UNIMPLEMENTED

The operation is not implemented or is not currently supported/enabled. HTTP Mapping: 501 Not Implemented Error Type: BAD_REQUEST

INVALID_ARGUMENT

The client specified an invalid argument. Note that this differs from

DEADLINE_EXCEEDED

The deadline expired before the operation could complete. For operations that change the state of the system, this error may be returned even if the operation has completed successfully. For example, a successful response from a server could have been delayed long enough for the deadline to expire. HTTP Mapping: 504 Gateway Timeout Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

SERVICE_ERROR

Service Error. There is a problem with an upstream service. This may be returned if a gateway receives an unknown error from a service or if a service is unreachable. If a request times out which waiting on a response from a service,

THROTTLED_CPU

Request throttled based on server CPU limits HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable. Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

THROTTLED_CONCURRENCY

Request throttled based on server concurrency limits. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 420 Enhance Your Calm Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

TOO_MANY_REQUESTS

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 429 Too Many Requests Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

TCP_FAILURE

Request failed due to network errors. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

MISSING_RESOURCE

Unable to perform operation because a required resource is missing. Example: Client is attempting to refresh a list, but the specified list is expired. This requires an action by the client to get a new list. If the user is simply trying GET a resource that is not found, use the NOT_FOUND error type. FAILED_PRECONDITION.MISSING_RESOURCE is to be used particularly when the user is performing an operation that requires a particular resource to exist. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request or 500 Internal Server Error Error Type: FAILED_PRECONDITION

ErrorType

Field

Description

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. For example, this error may be returned when an error code received from another address space belongs to an error space that is not known in this address space. Also errors raised by APIs that do not return enough error information may be converted to this error. If a client sees an unknown errorType, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. Unknown errors MUST NOT trigger any special behavior. These MAY be treated by an implementation as being equivalent to INTERNAL. When possible, a more specific error should be provided. HTTP Mapping: 520 Unknown Error

INTERNAL

Internal error. An unexpected internal error was encountered. This means that some invariants expected by the underlying system have been broken. This error code is reserved for serious errors. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

NOT_FOUND

The requested entity was not found. This could apply to a resource that has never existed (e.g. bad resource id), or a resource that no longer exists (e.g. cache expired.) Note to server developers: if a request is denied for an entire class of users, such as gradual feature rollout or undocumented allowlist,

UNAUTHENTICATED

The request does not have valid authentication credentials. This is intended to be returned only for routes that require authentication. HTTP Mapping: 401 Unauthorized

PERMISSION_DENIED

The caller does not have permission to execute the specified operation.

BAD_REQUEST

Bad Request. There is a problem with the request. Retrying the same request is not likely to succeed. An example would be a query or argument that cannot be deserialized. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request

UNAVAILABLE

Currently Unavailable. The service is currently unavailable. This is most likely a transient condition, which can be corrected by retrying with a backoff. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable

FAILED_PRECONDITION

The operation was rejected because the system is not in a state required for the operation's execution. For example, the directory to be deleted is non-empty, an rmdir operation is applied to a non-directory, etc. Service implementers can use the following guidelines to decide between

ParticipationStatus

Participation status of an entity (ie Player).

Field

Description

active

Entity (ie Player) actively participating.

inactive

Entity (ie Player) not actively participating anymore.

Scalars

Boolean

The Boolean scalar type represents true or false.

DateTime

DateTime formatted as ISO 8601

Duration

Duration formatted as ISO 8601

Float

The Float scalar type represents signed double-precision fractional values as specified by IEEE 754.

ID

The ID scalar type represents a unique identifier, often used to refetch an object or as key for a cache. The ID type appears in a JSON response as a String; however, it is not intended to be human-readable. When expected as an input type, any string (such as "4") or integer (such as 4) input value will be accepted as an ID.

Int

The Int scalar type represents non-fractional signed whole numeric values. Int can represent values between -(2^31) and 2^31 - 1.

String

The String scalar type represents textual data, represented as UTF-8 character sequences. The String type is most often used by GraphQL to represent free-form human-readable text.

Version

Version represented as string using format 'MAJOR.MINOR'

Series Events API

Transactions

A transaction is a single package of data sent over the WebSocket. It contains metadata (such as timestamps and sequence numbers) and an array of events. Transactions guarantee that all included events are processed together in the correct order, preserving the integrity of the series timeline.

Field Name

Type

Description

id

String

Unique ID of the transaction

correlationId

String

Internal reference for troubleshooting

occurredAt

String

ISO 8601 timestamp when the transaction occurred

publishedAt

String

ISO 8601 timestamp when the transaction was published to the WebSocket

seriesId

String

ID of the series

sequenceNumber

Int

Order of the transaction in the feed for the series (may skip if filtered)

sessionSequenceNumber

Int

Order of the transaction in the context of the current consumer session

events

Event[]

Array of one or more event objects (see below)

Events

An event is a single, discrete change or action that occurred within the series, such as a player kill, round start, or objective completion. Events include detailed information about the actor, action, target, and the resulting state change.

Field Name

Type

Description

id

String

Unique ID of the event

type

String

Event type in the format actor-action-target (e.g., player-killed-player)

includesFullState

Boolean

Whether the event includes the full state (based on configuration)

actor

Entity

The entity that performed the action

action

String

The action performed (e.g., killed, planted)

target

Entity

The entity affected by the action

seriesStateDelta

Object

The fields that changed at the series level as a result of this event

seriesState

Object

The complete series state after the event (if included)

revertedEventId

String?

(Optional) ID of the event that this event is reverting (only present for reverted events)

Events are structured as {actor}-{action}-{target} (e.g., player-killed-player). The API supports both shared (cross-title) and title-specific events.

Reverted Events

Any event can be reverted if an unexpected issue occurred (for example, due to an admin reset or technical reasons). A reverted event has the same structure as a normal event, but the action is prefixed with an exclamation mark (!), e.g., player-!killed-player.

The revertedEventId field points to the original event being reverted. The delta values in the reverted event are the inverse of the original (e.g., a kill count of -1 instead of +1).

Entity Fields

Field Name

Type

Description

type

String

Type of the entity (e.g., player, team, game)

id

String

Unique series-level entity ID

stateDelta

Object

Fields changed at the entity level

state

Object

Entity state after the event

Entity states are usually nested in one another, as can be seen here:

Series, which consists of

Games, which consist of

Segments (e.g., round), which consist of

Segments (e.g., buy phase) and so on

For clarity, events are grouped by their actor and action, with title-specific events marked accordingly.

GRID File Download API reference

The purpose of File Download API is to list and serve available files that are related to GRID entities.

Base URL:

https://api.grid.gg/file-download

Specifications

A comprehensive OpenAPI specification is available for download here.

Authentication

API Key (ApiKeyAuth)

Header provided API authentication key.

Parameter Name: x-api-key.

API Key (ApiKeyQueryParamAuth)

Query parameter provided API authentication key.

Parameter Name: key.

Endpoints

List Files

Check available files per Series.

Code sample

const headers = {

  'Accept':'application/json',

  'x-api-key':'API_KEY'

};

fetch('https://api.grid.gg/file-download/list/{series_id}',

{

  method: 'GET',

  headers: headers

})

.then(function(res) {

    return res.json();

}).then(function(body) {

    console.log(body);

});

GET /list/{series_id}

List all available files for Series with given ID

Parameters

Name

In

Type

Required

Description

series_id

path

string

true

The ID of the Series

Example responses

200 Response

{

  "files": [

    {

      "id": "string",

      "description": "string",

      "status": "string",

      "fileName": "string",

      "fullURL": "string"

    }

  ]

}

Responses

Status

Meaning

Description

Schema

200

OK

Successful operation

Inline

400

Bad Request

Required parameter has not been provided.

ApiErrorMessage

401

Unauthorized

Unauthorized request. Missing API key.

None

403

Forbidden

Forbidden access to the Series data.

None

5XX

Unknown

Server side processing issue.

ApiErrorMessage

Response Schema

Status Code 200

Name

Type

Required

Restrictions

Description

» files

FileInfo

false

none

none

»» id

string

false

none

File identification based on its type:

»» description

string

false

none

Short file description.

»» status

string

false

none

Status of the file:

»» fileName

string

false

none

Name of the file.

»» fullURL

string

false

none

File URL.

To perform this operation, you must be authenticated by means of one of the following methods: ApiKeyAuth, ApiKeyQueryParamAuth.

Download GRID Series Events File

Code sample

const headers = {

  'Accept':'application/zip',

  'x-api-key':'API_KEY'

};

fetch('https://api.grid.gg/file-download/events/grid/series/{series_id}',

{

  method: 'GET',

  headers: headers

})

.then(function(res) {

    return res.json();

}).then(function(body) {

    console.log(body);

});

Download GRID End State File

Code sample

const headers = {

  'Accept':'application/json',

  'x-api-key':'API_KEY'

};

fetch('https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/{series_id}',

{

  method: 'GET',

  headers: headers

})

.then(function(res) {

    return res.json();

}).then(function(body) {

    console.log(body);

});

File URL.

ApiErrorMessage

{

  "message": "string"

}

Properties

Name

Type

Required

Restrictions

Description

message

string

false

none

Error message.

Status

Name

Description

Notes

match-not-started

The series has not started. No file is available.

The related series has not started yet. The data will only become available after the game has been played out entirely.

match-in-progress

The series is in progress. No file is available.

Although the related series has started, no game has been completed yet. The data will only become available after the game has been played out entirely.

processing

The related file is being processed and not yet available for download.

Even though the game has been played out, it will take a few minutes for all of the data to get processed and be available for download. The data should become available soon

ready

The file can be downloaded.

 

file-not-available

The file is not available.

The related series has no related live data, nor is it expected to become available.

Enums

ErrorDetail

Field

Description

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. This error should only be returned when no other error detail applies. If a client sees an unknown errorDetail, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

FIELD_NOT_FOUND

The requested field is not found in the schema. This differs from

INVALID_CURSOR

The provided cursor is not valid. The most common usage for this error is when a client is paginating through a list that uses stateful cursors. In that case, the provided cursor may be expired. HTTP Mapping: 404 Not Found Error Type: NOT_FOUND

UNIMPLEMENTED

The operation is not implemented or is not currently supported/enabled. HTTP Mapping: 501 Not Implemented Error Type: BAD_REQUEST

INVALID_ARGUMENT

The client specified an invalid argument. Note that this differs from

DEADLINE_EXCEEDED

The deadline expired before the operation could complete. For operations that change the state of the system, this error may be returned even if the operation has completed successfully. For example, a successful response from a server could have been delayed long enough for the deadline to expire. HTTP Mapping: 504 Gateway Timeout Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

SERVICE_ERROR

Service Error. There is a problem with an upstream service. This may be returned if a gateway receives an unknown error from a service or if a service is unreachable. If a request times out which waiting on a response from a service,

THROTTLED_CPU

Request throttled based on server CPU limits HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable. Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

THROTTLED_CONCURRENCY

Request throttled based on server concurrency limits. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 420 Enhance Your Calm Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

TOO_MANY_REQUESTS

The server detected that the client is exhibiting a behavior that might be generating excessive load. HTTP Mapping: 429 Too Many Requests Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

TCP_FAILURE

Request failed due to network errors. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable Error Type: UNAVAILABLE

MISSING_RESOURCE

Unable to perform operation because a required resource is missing. Example: Client is attempting to refresh a list, but the specified list is expired. This requires an action by the client to get a new list. If the user is simply trying GET a resource that is not found, use the NOT_FOUND error type. FAILED_PRECONDITION.MISSING_RESOURCE is to be used particularly when the user is performing an operation that requires a particular resource to exist. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request or 500 Internal Server Error Error Type: FAILED_PRECONDITION

ErrorType

Field

Description

UNKNOWN

Unknown error. For example, this error may be returned when an error code received from another address space belongs to an error space that is not known in this address space. Also errors raised by APIs that do not return enough error information may be converted to this error. If a client sees an unknown errorType, it will be interpreted as UNKNOWN. Unknown errors MUST NOT trigger any special behavior. These MAY be treated by an implementation as being equivalent to INTERNAL. When possible, a more specific error should be provided. HTTP Mapping: 520 Unknown Error

INTERNAL

Internal error. An unexpected internal error was encountered. This means that some invariants expected by the underlying system have been broken. This error code is reserved for serious errors. HTTP Mapping: 500 Internal Server Error

NOT_FOUND

The requested entity was not found. This could apply to a resource that has never existed (e.g. bad resource id), or a resource that no longer exists (e.g. cache expired.) Note to server developers: if a request is denied for an entire class of users, such as gradual feature rollout or undocumented allowlist,

UNAUTHENTICATED

The request does not have valid authentication credentials. This is intended to be returned only for routes that require authentication. HTTP Mapping: 401 Unauthorized

PERMISSION_DENIED

The caller does not have permission to execute the specified operation.

BAD_REQUEST

Bad Request. There is a problem with the request. Retrying the same request is not likely to succeed. An example would be a query or argument that cannot be deserialized. HTTP Mapping: 400 Bad Request

UNAVAILABLE

Currently Unavailable. The service is currently unavailable. This is most likely a transient condition, which can be corrected by retrying with a backoff. HTTP Mapping: 503 Unavailable

FAILED_PRECONDITION

The operation was rejected because the system is not in a state required for the operation's execution. For example, the directory to be deleted is non-empty, an rmdir operation is applied to a non-directory, etc. Service implementers can use the following guidelines to decide between

Scalars

Boolean

The Boolean scalar type represents true or false.

Duration

Float

The Float scalar type represents signed double-precision fractional values as specified by IEEE 754.

ID

The ID scalar type represents a unique identifier, often used to refetch an object or as key for a cache. The ID type appears in a JSON response as a String; however, it is not intended to be human-readable. When expected as an input type, any string (such as "4") or integer (such as 4) input value will be accepted as an ID.

Int

The Int scalar type represents non-fractional signed whole numeric values. Int can represent values between -(2^31) and 2^31 - 1.

String

The String scalar type represents textual data, represented as UTF-8 character sequences. The String type is most often used by GraphQL to represent free-form human-readable text.

Widget Overview

GRID Widget embeds allow you to display series, game, and tournament data directly on your website using official GRID data feeds. Widgets are highly configurable, supporting multiple integration methods, internationalization, advanced theming, delay control, and both internal and external data sources. Integration can be customized for different frameworks, with widget types spanning scoreboards, tables, data visualizations, live logs, streams, and map overlays

Available Widget Types

Type

Description

game-overview

A one widget solution with a comprehensive overview of the current state including a minimap

series-scoreboard

Multi-team series scoreboard

series-team-scoreboard

Scoreboard for a specific team in a series

stream

Secure video streaming player

series-timeline

Visual event timeline

series-livelog

Real-time event log

series-table

Tabular entity, player, or team statistics

series-comparison

Comparison chart between entities, teams, or stats

series-map-schematic

Game minimap or schematic with overlays

seriesNetWorth

DOTA net worth visualization

feedStatus

Displays real-time feed and data status

series-live-predictions

Displays real-time win predictions for live series

Integration Approaches

Widgets can be integrated in two primary ways:

Plain JavaScript embed:

Insert the embed script from the GRID CDN and initialize the widget using the provided API.

React Package:

Dynamically load the script and invoke the loadWidget method at the appropriate lifecycle moment with the same properties as in plain JavaScript.

Delays

Widgets use the official broadcast delay by default but may be set to non-delayed (zero) mode for overlays. In non-delayed mode, some sensitive data is omitted for competitive integrity. Secure usage of API keys is required for non-delayed or overlay contexts, and API keys must never be exposed publicly.

External Data Provider Support

Pass a function to the dataProvider property to push a fully custom state into the widget (not using GRID live data). The function receives a setState handler to update widget content at any time. All provided data must match the exact expected state schema for that widget.

Translation and Localization Support

The widget system is built to support flexible internationalization out of the box. All user-visible content within widgets—such as labels, tooltips, section titles, and dynamic messages—can be localized to suit the needs of different audiences and geographic regions. Use the lang property to change the language and the formatting of dates and times. We are using the i18next framework which also allows further customization of particular strings using the translate property.

Widgets Quick-start guide

This guide outlines the fastest way to embed and configure GRID Widgets in your web application, covering both vanilla JavaScript and framework-based integrations. It also highlights required properties, basic customization, and notes for secure deployment.

Embedding a Widget Using JavaScript

Include the GRID Widget Library

Add the GRID Widget script from the CDN in your HTML file

<script type="text/javascript" src="https://cdn.grid.gg/widgets/latest/embed.js"></script>

Add a Container Element

Create a DOM element where the widget will render

<div id="widget1" style="height: 200px"></div>

Initialize the Widget

Call the loadWidget method with the desired configuration

window.grid.loadWidget({

  el: document.getElementById('widget1'),

  type: 'series-scoreboard',

  scope: { id: 1 },            

  });

The scope object is mandatory and must match the widget type (e.g., containing a series or tournament ID).

Widget Basic Configuration

grid:loadWidget function

Methods

loadWidget(settings: object): void

Method used to load the widget once you are ready to render it within your apps lifecycle methods. It accepts a settings object defined below of the various options available.

Widget Translations

All widgets can be translated to any language. To display content in other languages you need to prepare translations and add 2 parameters to the widget options object: “lang” and “translation”. See details below.

Name

Description

Type

lang

language code. Controls local date/time formatting. Examples: “it”, “de”, “en”, “ru”, “cz”

List of ISO 639 language codes - Wikipedia

translation

Snake case strings that represent the visible widget content. See more details here:

Code example

window.grid.loadWidget({

    el: document.getElementById('series-table'),

    type: 'series-table',

    scope: {

        type: 'series',

        id: 1,

    },

    options: {

        lang: 'be',

        translation: {

            statistics: 'Статыстыка',

            reset_table: 'Вярнуць да пачатковага стану',

            edit_columns: 'Рэдагаваць слупкі',

            player: 'Гулец',

            team: 'Каманда',

            team_summary: 'Залік каманды',

            series_info: 'Інфармацыя па серыі',

            series: 'Серыя'

        },

    },

});

Base colors

Base Color is either a string, and then we generate the correct tints for your, or alternatively you can pass your own as an object of tints, these should be in the following format. Where 100 is the solid color, and each step is a 5% decrement of the tint.

You can use https://noeldelgado.github.io/shadowlord/#13191e to generate these tints.

base: {

  100: '#080a0c', // shadows

    95: 'orange', // dark backgrounds (team scoreboard widget - items)

    90: '#fff', // backgrounds

    85: 'yellow', // borders

    80: 'purple', // scrollbars, horizontal lines

    75: 'green',

    70: 'banana', // light horizontal separator (live log),

    65: '#ddd',

    60: 'green', // texts, icons

    55: 'gray',

    50: 'red',

    45: '#ff0033',

    40: 'green', // light text, video controls

    35: 'red',

    30: 'red',

    25: '#11171b',

    20: '#aa229f', // text

    15: 'red',

    10: 'red',

    5: 'red',

    0: '#0f1418' // strong text

},

Sample costume widget theme

window.onload = function () {

                window.grid.loadWidget({

                    el: document.getElementById('root'),

                    type: 'seriesNetWorth',

                    foo: 'bar',

                    scope: {

                        type: 'series',

                        id: 1,

                    },

                    theme: {

                        fonts: ['cursive', 'cursive'],

                        fontImportUrl:

                            "@import url('https://fonts.googleapis.com/css?family=cursive&display=swap');",

                        radii: [50, 50],

                        colors: {

                            base: { 90: '#592f55' },

                        },

                        widgetContainer: {

                            border: '4px solid',

                            showHeader: true,

                            headerColor: '#afaf7a',

                        },

                    },

                    options: {

                        teamColorType: 'team',

                    },

                });

}

Widget Data Source and Delay

Our widget can be used with internal (GRID) and external data.

Internal data source

To use our widgets with GRID data on your own website you need to do the following:

Contact GRID to add your domain in whitelist (localhost is in whitelist)

Configure widget scope. You need to set data type and particular id

window.grid.loadWidget({

     el: document.getElementById('widget1'),

     type: 'series-scoreboard',

     scope: {

       type: 'series',

       id: 42,

     },

   });

Non-Delayed Live Data (Integrity Safe Widgets) (Optional)

There is an option to enable non-delayed data on the widgets. When non-delayed data is enabled, all in-game events will be displayed without any delay on the widgets. However, having this feature enabled excludes several data points as they can potentially cause integrity risk.

Supported Integrity Safe Widgets

Game Overview

Series Scoreboard

Live Log

Timeline

Table

Comparison

Team Scoreboard

Team Net Worth

Status

How to enable non-delayed live data

To enable non-delayed data, set the "delay" property to "zero" in the options object. This property supports "public" for broadcast speed data or "zero" for live data (excluding some events).

window.grid.loadWidget({

     el: document.getElementById('widget1'),

     type: 'series-scoreboard',

     scope: {

       type: 'series',

       id: 42,

     },

      delay: "zero"

   });

External data source

This option enables you to use our widgets across your portfolio with any data you pass to them even if not supplied by GRID.

Widgets with external data source support

Series Scoreboard

Live Log

Timeline

Table

Comparison

Team Scoreboard

Team Net Worth

Status

How to enable an external data source

To use widgets with external data (powered by you) you need to pass a function and use it to set the widget state completely from your side. Here is an example:

   function externalDataSource(setState) {

     setState({

       data,

       teamColors,

       delay: 0,

       loading: false,

       reconnecting: false,

       error: null,

     });

   }

   window.grid.loadWidget({

     el: 'widget2',

     type: 'series-scoreboard',

     scope: {

       type: 'series',

     },

     options: {

       dataProvider: externalDataSource,

     }

   });

 };

</script>

Type

Changes background color of widget container. Any css supported color like "#ff00ff" or "yellow".

GRID powered widget options

Name

Description

Type

teamColorType

Team color type indicates whether to use team's branding colors or the current title's side colors. The "team" type informs the widget that the colors need to be based on teams’ branding. For example, Fnatic's branding color is orange, which means, their color will be orange. The "side" type tells the widget that the colors need to be based on teams' sides in the game. (i.e CT - Blue, T - Yellow in CSGO)

enum "team" / "side"

apiKey

This key should only be used when the widget is set to "delay: 0" and only in an overlay context. Using it in other contexts will expose your private key publicly. You can find the API key for authorization in your Grid account.

string

delay

Defines what delay is used for the widget. More info available in Data sources and delays

CustomDataPoint

Name

Description

Type

dataPoint*

Corresponds to the string value of a standard DataPoint. Specifies the statistic to be visualized within the widget.

string

displayName*

Allows you to specify a custom name for the dataPoint. Provided displayName will be used in any visualization styles you choose, providing a more meaningful and user-friendly label for the data point.

string

dataSelectionId

Provides a method for accessing specific subsets of filtered data from dataSelection, used when working with conversion rates statistics. The dataSelectionId should be set to the ID of a specific dataSelection item from which statistics will be retrieved.How to set up conversion rates?

string

Example

{

 dataPoint: "won.[value=true].percentage",

 displayName: "Percentage of Wins at Vertigo",

 dataSelectionId: "statisticsFromVertigo",

},

dataPoints convention

DataPoints are strings used to access values from a nested data structure of Stats Feed API. They allow you to specify precisely what data you want to show within the table, even when dealing with complex and deeply nested data.

Examples of dataPoints

kills.avg

This dataPoint points to kills in the data structure and retrieves the value associated with the avg key within.

deaths.avg

Similar to kills.avg, this dataPoint navigates to the deaths key and retrieves the avg value within deaths.

wins.[value=true].sum

This dataPoint handles a conditional extraction. It navigates to the wins key, which is expected to be a list of properties containing value property which is boolean. It then filters this list to include only those dictionaries where value is true and retrieves the sum property value.

Note: To see the whole list of available statistics visit our Portal Documentation (API Overview, API Reference) regarding Stats Feed API query from where this data is coming from. Please remember that query name is already provided same with sampling

Creating Your Own dataPoints

To create your own dataPoints, follow these guidelines:

Dot Notation

Use dots (.) to navigate through the keys of nested objects.

Example: To access the killAssistsGiven avg in a nested dictionary { killAssistsGiven: { avg: 3.45 } }, use killAssistsGiven.avg

Conditionals

Use square brackets ([]) to specify conditions for lists of dictionaries.

Format: key.[condition_key=condition_value].value

Example: If you have a list of dictionaries under the key objectives, and you want to extract entries where type is defuseBomb and then access sum. Which is nested 1 level deeper within completionCount. Datapoint would look like objectives.[type=defuseBomb].completionCount.sum

How to set up conversion rates?

Conversion rates allow us to select statistics only when some filter is true. For example we can select statistics collected only on one or multiple maps for teams. Example of this would this dataSelection item that selects only statistics when on map “mirage” and then shows wins percentage at this map:

{

 id: "mirageMap",

 filter: {

   map: {

     name: {

       contains: "mirage",

     },

   },

 },

}

This then corresponds to setting up CustomDataPoint which has to contain appropriate to dataSelection item, key id.Example of this “dataPoint” would be as:

{

 dataPoint: "won.[value=true].percentage",

 displayName: "Percentage of Wins at Mirage",

 dataSelectionId: "mirageMap",

},

As you can see dataSelectionId has to match id of dataSelection to properly select filtered data. displayName can be whatever you feel is the best at representing this statistic.

List of all available statistics can be accessed through Portal Documentation

State

The widget doesn’t support external data.

Video Overview

GRID offers three primary video delivery solutions for esports: the Video Stream Widget for rapid website embedding, the HLS Video Stream API for programmatic, low-latency playback in custom players, and Direct RTMP Video Distribution for ingesting live video streams into custom CDN or broadcast workflows. Each serves different integration needs:

Solution

Pros

Video Stream Widget

Fastest embed; zero-setup; easy theming and built-in access control.

HLS Video Stream API

Full control over playback; API-based and compatible with any HLS-enabled player.

Direct RTMP Distribution

Professional, ultra-low-latency streaming; suitable for custom CDN workflows.

RTMP Video Getting Started

Prerequisites: GRID API key, CDN/RTMP infrastructure.

Best For: Advanced broadcast, distribution, or multi-venue streaming needs where direct stream ingest is required.

RTMP Video Quick-Start Guide

1. Discover RTMP Endpoint

Get Series Channel:

GET https://api.grid.gg/video-outgestion/channels/series/<series_id>?key=<api-key>

Response Example:

{

  "id": "<channel-id>",

  "rtmpPullEndpoint": "rtmp://ds-outgest-01.grid.gg:1935/live/<channel-ext>?seriesId=<series id>"

}

2. Connect Player or CDN

Use the provided rtmpPullEndpoint (with key=<api-key>) as the RTMP source in your media infrastructure.

Common

Guidelines

API keys and token generation must always remain backend-only for security.

Use GRID’s Central Data API to obtain valid seriesId values.

For technical support or advanced use cases, contact dcsm@grid.gg.

HLS Video Getting Started

The HLS Video Stream API provides direct access to GRID's live esports video streams for playback in your custom frontend player or application.

Prerequisites: GRID API key, customer ID, series ID, backend component for token generation.

Best For: Developers wanting fine-grained control over the video player interface and experience in any HLS-compatible environment.

HLS Video Quick-Start Guide

1. Generate a Viewer Token

Endpoint:

POST https://api.grid.gg/widgets/video-token-generator/token/generate?key=<api-key>

Payload:

{

  "seriesId": "<series-id>",

  "customerId": "<customer-id>",

  "userId": "<unique-user-id>"

}

Response:

{ "token": "<jwt-token>" }

2. Retrieve Video URL

Endpoint:

GET https://api.grid.gg/b2c/video-stream-coordinator/streams/<seriesId>

Headers:

video-token: <jwt-token>

Response Example:

{

  "isOffline": false,

  "status": "OK",

  "url": "<hls-video-url>"

}

3. Play in HLS Player

Use the returned url as the video source in any HLS-compatible player (e.g., hls.js, Video.js, JWPlayer).

4. Refresh Token

Periodically refresh the JWT (token expires every few minutes):

Endpoint:

GET https://api.grid.gg/widgets/video-token-generator/verify

Headers:

video-token: <current-jwt>

New token is received in the response headers.

5. Revoke User Access

Endpoint:

POST https://api.grid.gg/widgets/video-token-generator/token/revoke?key=<api-key>

Payload:

{ "customerId": "<customer-id>", "userId": "<unique-user-id>" }

Video Widget Getting Started

Prerequisites: GRID API key, customer ID, series ID, ability to make backend calls.

Best For: Teams needing fast, branded, frontend video embedding with built-in theming and access control.

Video Widget Quick-Start Guide

1. Generate a User Token

Endpoint:

POST https://api.grid.gg/widgets/video-token-generator/token/generate?key=<api-key>

Payload:

{

  "seriesId": "<series-id>",

  "customerId": "<customer-id>",

  "userId": "<unique-user-id>"

}

Response:

{ "token": "<jwt-token>" }

2. Embed the Widget

JavaScript Example:

import { loadWidget } from '@grid-esports/widget-sdk';

loadWidget({

  el: "root",

  type: 'stream',

  scope: { type: 'series', id: '<series-id>' },

  options: { token: '<jwt-token>' }

});

4. Revoke User Access

Endpoint:

POST https://api.grid.gg/widgets/video-token-generator/token/revoke?key=<api-key>

Payload:

{ "customerId": "<customer-id>", "userId": "<unique-user-id>" }

Styling and properties

You can find more information about widget styling and other properties in the Widget Documentation

Authenticating Your API Requests

If you have encountered the dreaded 401 (unauthorized error), you might need some help figuring out the proper way to authenticate your API requests. Read on for the info you need!

There are two ways to authenticate your API requests. You can either pass the API key into your request as a header, or you can include it in the URL as a request parameter. Note that request headers are a better way to keep your API key secure than request parameters.

NOTE: If you don’t know your API key, ask the admin user for your team to find it in the Account Management > Users area. If you are the admin, you can find Account Management at the bottom of the left navigation bar. Click “View” on the appropriate user in the list, then click where it says “API Keys” to view that user’s API key.

Using Request Headers

Your API key can be sent as part of your request using an “x-api-key” header. See the examples below. In these examples, we are downloading the GRID-formatted end-state data for series ID 2589176.

Python

Below is an example API request, using the built-in requests module.

import requests

headers = {

    "x-api-key": "YOUR_API_KEY"

}

response = requests.get(

    "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176",

    headers = headers

)

JavaScript

Below is an example API request in JavaScript, using the axios package.

const axios = require('axios');

axios.get('https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176', {

    headers: {

       ‘x-api-key’: ‘YOUR_API_KEY’

    }

})

  .then(response => {

    // Interact with the response object as necessary

    // The response body will be contained within response.data

  });

Curl

You can use headers to authenticate a curl request as follows:

curl https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176 -H "x-api-key: YOUR_API_KEY"

Minor variations in curl syntax may be necessary on different platforms (Linux vs. macOS vs. Windows).

Using Request Parameters

Your API key can also be sent using a URL parameter, though this is a less secure method. See the examples below. In these examples, we are downloading the GRID-formatted end-state data for series ID 2589176.

Python

Below is an example API request, using the built-in requests module.

import requests

response = requests.get(

    "https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176?key={YOUR_API_KEY}"

)

JavaScript

Below is an example API request in JavaScript, using the axios package.

const axios = require('axios');

axios.get(

    'https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176?key=YOUR_API_KEY'

  ).then(response => {

    // Interact with the response object as necessary

    // The response body will be contained within response.data

  });

Curl

You can use a request parameter to authenticate a curl request as follows:

curl https://api.grid.gg/file-download/end-state/grid/series/2589176?key=YOUR_API_KEY

Fetching Lists of Series from the GRID API

Before you can fetch and use the in-game data for the matches available on the GRID Platform (for example, to download your scrim files if you belong to a professional team), you will need to find a list of series IDs for your code to work through. Here's how to get that list, using GRID's Central Data API.

Central Data is a GraphQL API that contains GRID's "static data", such as data about teams, players, tournaments, and series.

For details about how to work with GRID's GraphQL APIs, including details around pagination, rate limiting, and errors, see the GraphQL API Reference documentation.

Preparing and Sending Your Query

To get a list of series that meet certain criteria, we'll use the allSeries query.

Here's a basic example of a simple allSeries query that fetches the most recent 50 Valorant esports series.

In this example, we have used filters to request only VALORANT series and only "esports" series (no scrims).

Endpoint: https://api.grid.gg/central-data/graphql

{

    allSeries (

        first: 50,

        filter: {

            titleId: 6  # Valorant

            types: ESPORTS  # Esports matches only

        }

        orderBy: StartTimeScheduled  # Sort by start time

        orderDirection: DESC  # Sort by most recent first

    ) {

        totalCount

        pageInfo {

            hasPreviousPage

            hasNextPage

            startCursor

            endCursor

        }

        edges {

            node {

                id

                title {

                    id

                }

                tournament {

                    id

                    name

                }

            }

        }

    }

}

Parameters and Filters in this Query

The first: 50 parameter specifies that we want to receive 50 results per page, which is the maximum allowed.

Filters

filter: {

    titleId: 6

    types: ESPORTS

}

The titleId: 6 portion requests the Valorant game title. See below for title IDs for other game titles.

The types: ESPORTS portion requests only esports series (no scrims).

Finally, orderBy: StartTimeScheduled sorts the response by start time, and orderDirection: DESC asks it so sort the most recent first (descending order).

Response Fields in this Query

The totalCount field asks the query to show us how many total series are available using these filters.

pageInfo {

    hasPreviousPage

    hasNextPage

    startCursor

    endCursor

}

These pagination fields give us useful information about which page we are viewing within all of the available pages of results. More on that later!

edges {

    node {

        id

        tournament {

            id

            name

        }

    }

}

This portion of the query asks GraphQL to send us information about each series as an array of "nodes." For more on what "edges" and "nodes" are in GraphQL, see the official documentation.

Within each node, we are asking for the id of the series and the id and name of the tournament to which it belongs. Several other fields are available for series nodes, as listed here.

Filters

There are several different filters you can use to ensure that you are finding all of the series you are interested in, and only the series you are interested in.

To use a filter, simply add it on a line inside the filter: {} portion of your query. Some commonly useful filters are described below, with a complete list available here.

titleId

This filters the result by game title. For example, you can use these values:

VALORANT - 6

LOL - 3

Rainbow 6: Siege - 25

For a complete list of title IDs, see the API Reference.

types

Available series types include ESPORTS (official matches), SCRIM (private practice matches), and COMPETITIVE (Champions Queue).

startTimeScheduled The time the series was scheduled to begin, using UTC. To use this filter, you must provide either a gte paramter ("greater than or equal"), an lte paramater ("less than or equal"), or both. For example, to find series that started between January 1, 2023 and December 31, 2023, you could use this filter:

startTimeScheduled: {

    gte: "2023-01-01T00:00:00Z"

    lte: "2023-12-31T00:00:00Z"

}

productServiceLevels

This filter can restrict the results to only show games with certain levels of available data. For example, to only return series with complete live data, you could use this filter:

productServiceLevels: {

    productName: "liveDataFeed"

    serviceLevel: FULL

}

Pagination

Since you can only retrieve 50 records at a time, you may need to submit many queries to fetch a complete list of series that match your filters. You can do this using query pagination.

For a detailed guide to using pagination in your queries, see the GraphQL API Reference documentation.

Welcome to Sky’s the Limit - Cloud9 x JetBrains Hackathon

Cloud9 is bringing its competitive spirit from the arena to the dev world—with a global hackathon built to ignite creativity, sharpen skills, and bring bold ideas to life. As one of the most storied organizations in esports, Cloud9 is known for championship rosters, fierce innovation, and a community that pushes the boundaries of what’s possible. Whether you’re a gamer, a builder, or a curious creator, this is your chance to level up alongside a team that never stops evolving.

In this hackathon, entrants will build or update a working application using the tools of their choice—plus optional support from JetBrains’ AI Coding Agent, Junie. Junie can help accelerate your workflow and unlock new ways to create, but the real spotlight is on you and the ideas you bring to the table.

With exclusive resources like official esports data for League of Legends and VALORANT provided by GRID, expert guidance, and a prize pool that rewards innovation, this is your arena. Pick a category, lock in, and show Cloud9 what you can build.

Why join?

Experiment with JetBrains IDEs + AI Coding Agent Junie

Official data provided by GRID

Compete for $25k cash prizes, GDC tickets + travel, and Cloud9 swag

Get Started

Review our Submission Specifics tab

Apply here to get access to the official esports data from GRID

Download and open your JetBrains IDE and start coding!

Learn how to create an AI-powered app with AI Coding Agent Junie

Requirements

What to Build

Entrants must build or update a working application that uses JetBrains IDEs and Junie and submit it into one of the following categories:

Category 1 - A comprehensive Assistant Coach powered by Data Science and AI: that merges micro-level player analytics with macro-level strategic review. Inspired by Moneyball (Jonah Hill’s Peter Brand), this near-real-time application analyzes historical match data to provide a holistic and actionable review. The platform crunches the numbers to identify recurring individual mistakes and connects them directly to their impact on team-wide macro strategy, generating targeted insights for coaches and players.

Category 2 - Automated Scouting Report Generator: An application that, given an upcoming opponent, automatically scours GRID data from their recent matches to generate a concise scouting report. The report would highlight common strategies, player tendencies, and default site setups (for VAL), or recently played comps (for LoL & VAL).

Category 3 - AI Drafting Assistant/Drafting Predictor (LoL): Develop a tool that analyzes historical GRID data (team compositions, player champion/agent pools, win rates, champion synergies, patch data, recent games history) to recommend optimal draft strategies, picks, and bans against specific opponents in real-time during the pick/ban phase.

Category 4 - Event Game: Develop a mini-game that can be played by fans at a LCS or VCT Event Booth or Finals Activation. The winning project will be integrated into a future Cloud9 & JetBrains Event Booth.

Please read through the Submission Specifics page for full details.

What to Submit

Provide a URL to your code repository for judging and testing.

The repository must contain all necessary source code, assets, and instructions required for the project to be functional. The repository must be public with an approved OSI Open Source License in the About Me section. 

Include a video (about 3 minutes) that demonstrates your submission. Videos must be uploaded to YouTube, Vimeo, or Facebook Video and made public.

Identify which category you are submitting into.

Fully completed Devpost submission form.

Please check the Official Rules for full details.

Judging Criteria

Technological Implementation

Does the project demonstrate quality software development? Does the project leverage the JetBrains IDEs or AI Coding Agent Junie (encouraged)? How is the quality of the code?

Design

Is the user experience and design of the project well thought out?

Potential Impact

How big of an impact could the project have on the specific community or target audience?

Quality of the Idea

How creative and unique is the project?

Sky’s the Limit - Cloud9 x JetBrains Hackathon (the “Hackathon”) Official Rules

NO PURCHASE OR PAYMENT NECESSARY TO ENTER OR WIN. A PURCHASE OR PAYMENT WILL NOT INCREASE YOUR CHANCES OF WINNING. 

SUBMISSION OF ANY ENTRY CONSTITUTES AGREEMENT TO THESE OFFICIAL RULES AS A CONTRACT BETWEEN ENTRANT (AND EACH INDIVIDUAL MEMBER OF ENTRANT), THE HACKATHON SPONSOR, AND DEVPOST.

SUBJECT TO ALL FEDERAL, STATE, MUNICIPAL, AND LOCAL LAWS, REGULATIONS, AND ORDINANCES. VOID WHERE PROHIBITED BY LAW.

 

1. Dates and Timing

Registration & Submission Period: December 9, 2025 (11:00 am Pacific Time) – February 3, 2026 (11:00 am Pacific Time) (“Registration & Submission Period”).

Judging Period: February 10, 2026 (12:00 pm Pacific Time) – February 24, 2026 (12:00 pm PacificTime) (“Judging Period”).

Winners Announced: On or around March 9, 2026 (11:00 am Pacific Time).

The official timekeeping clock shall be Sponsor’s clock. Entries must be received within the Registration & Submission Period to be eligible.

2. Sponsor and Administrator

Sponsor: Cloud9 Esports, Inc., 2720 Neilson Way, 5697, Santa Monica, California, 90409

Administrator: Devpost, Inc. (“Devpost”), 222 Broadway, Floor 19, New York, NY 10038

 

3. Eligibility

The Hackathon IS open to: 

Individuals who are at least the age of majority where they reside as of the time of entry (“Eligible Individuals”);

Teams of Eligible Individuals (“Teams”); and

Organizations (including corporations, not-for-profit corporations and other nonprofit organizations, limited liability companies, partnerships, and other legal entities) that exist and have been organized or incorporated at the time of entry.

(the above are collectively, “Entrants”)

An Eligible Individual may join more than one Team or Organization and an Eligible Individual who is part of a Team or Organization may also enter the Hackathon on an individual basis. If a Team or Organization is entering the Hackathon, they must appoint and authorize one individual (the “Representative”) to represent, act, and enter a Submission, on their behalf. By entering a Submission on behalf of a Team or Organization you represent and warrant that you are the Representative authorized to act on behalf of your Team or Organization.

The Hackathon IS NOT open to: 

Individuals who are residents of, or Organizations domiciled in, a country, state, province or territory where the laws of the United States or local law prohibits participating or receiving a prize in the Hackathon (including, but not limited to, Brazil, Quebec, Russia, Crimea, Cuba, Iran, North Korea, Syria and any other country designated by the United States Treasury's Office of Foreign Assets Control) 

Organizations involved with the design, production, paid promotion, execution, or distribution of the Hackathon, including the Sponsor and Administrator (“Promotion Entities”).

Employees, representatives and agents** of such Promotion Entities, and all members of their immediate family or household*

Any other individual involved with the design, production, promotion, execution, or distribution of the Hackathon, and each member of their immediate family or household*

Any Judge (defined below), or company or individual that employs a Judge

Any parent company, subsidiary, or other affiliate*** of any organization described above

Any other individual or organization whose participation in the Hackathon would create, in the sole discretion of the Sponsor and/or Administrator, a real or apparent conflict of interest 

*The members of an individual’s immediate family include the individual’s spouse, children and stepchildren, parents and stepparents, and siblings and stepsiblings. The members of an individual’s household include any other person that shares the same residence as the individual for at least three (3) months out of the year. 

**Agents include individuals or organizations that in creating a Submission to the Hackathon, are acting on behalf of, and at the direction of, a Promotion Entity through a contractual or similar relationship.

***An affiliate is: (a) an organization that is under common control, sharing a common majority or controlling owner, or common management; or (b) an organization that has a substantial ownership in, or is substantially owned by the other organization.

 

4. How To Enter 

Entrants may enter by visiting cloud9.devpost.com (“Hackathon Website”) and following the below steps:

Register for the Hackathon on the Hackathon Website by clicking the “Join Hackathon” button. To complete registration, sign up to create a free Devpost account, or log in with an existing Devpost account. This will enable you to receive important updates and to create your Submission.

Entrants will obtain access to the required developer tools/platform and complete a Project described below in Project Requirements. Use of the developer tools will be subject to the license agreement related thereto. Entry in the Hackathon constitutes consent for the Sponsor and Devpost to collect and maintain an entrant’s personal information for the purpose of operating and publicizing the Hackathon.

Complete and enter all of the required fields on the “Enter a Submission” page of the Hackathon Website (each a “Submission”) during the Submission Period and follow the requirements below.

Project Requirements

What to Create: Entrants must build or update a working application and are encouraged to use JetBrains IDEs and AI Coding Agent Junie to submit it into one of the following categories (each a “Project”).

Categories:

Category 1: A Comprehensive Assistant Coach: that merges micro-level player analytics with macro-level strategic review. Inspired by Moneyball (Jonah Hill’s Peter Brand), this near-real-time application analyzes alongside historical match data to provide a holistic and actionable review. The platform crunches the numbers to identify recurring individual mistakes and connects them directly to their impact on team-wide macro strategy, generating targeted insights for coaches and players.

Category 2: Automated Scouting Report Generator: An application that, given an upcoming opponent, automatically scours GRID data from their recent matches to generate a concise scouting report. The report could highlight common strategies, player tendencies, and default site setups (for VALORANT), or recently played comps (for VALORANT or League of Legends). 

Category 3: AI Drafting Assistant/Drafting Predictor (League of Legends): Develop a tool that analyzes historical GRID data (team compositions, player champion/agent pools, win rates, champion synergies, patch data, recent games history) to recommend optimal draft strategies, picks, and bans against specific opponents in real-time during the pick/ban phase. 

Category 4: Event Game: Develop a mini-game that can be played by fans at a LCS or VCT event booth or finals activation. The winning project will be integrated into a future Cloud9 & JetBrains event booth at Cloud9’s sole and absolute discretion.

Functionality: The Project must be capable of being successfully installed and running consistently on the platform for which it is intended and must function as depicted in the video and/or expressed in the text description.

Platforms: A submitted Project must run on the platform for which it is intended and which is specified in the Submission Requirements. 

New & Existing: Projects must be either newly created by the Entrant or, if the Entrant’s Project existed prior to the Hackathon Submission Period, must have significantly updated after the start of the Hackathon Submission Period. Entrants should explain how their Project was significantly updated during the Submission Period.

Third Party Integrations: If a Project integrates any third-party SDK, APIs and/or data, Entrant must be authorized to use them in accordance with any terms and conditions or licensing requirements of the tool.

 

Submission Requirements 

Submissions to the Hackathon must meet the following requirements:

Include a Project built with the required developer tools and meets the above Project Requirements.

Provide a URL to your code repository for judging and testing. The repository must contain all necessary source code, assets, and instructions required for the project to be functional. The repository must be public and open source by including an open source license file. This license should be detectable and visible at the top of the repository page (in the About section).  

Include which category you are submitting to. 

Include a text description that should explain the features and functionality of your Project.

Include a demonstration video of your Project. The video portion of the Submission:

should be less than three (3) minutes. Judges are not required to watch beyond three minutes 

should include footage that shows the Project functioning on the device for which it was built

must be uploaded to and made publicly visible on YouTube, Vimeo, Facebook Video, or Youku, and a link to the video must be provided on the submission form on the Hackathon Website; and

must not include third party trademarks, or copyrighted music or other material unless the Entrant has permission to use such material.

Multiple Submissions 

An Entrant may submit more than one Submission, however, each Submission must be unique and substantially different from each of the Entrant’s other Submissions, as determined by the Sponsor and Devpost in their sole discretion.

Submission ownership

Submissions must be the original work of the Entrant, be solely owned by the Entrant, and not violate the IP rights of any other person or entity.

 

Testing 

Access must be provided to an Entrant’s working Project for judging and testing by providing a link to a website, functioning demo, or a test build. If Entrant’s website is private, Entrant must include login credentials in its testing instructions. The Entrant must make the Project available free of charge and without any restriction, for testing, evaluation and use by the Sponsor, Administrator and Judges until the Judging Period ends. Judges are not required to test the Project and may choose to judge based solely on the text description, images, and video provided in the Submission.

If the Project includes software that runs on proprietary or third party hardware that is not widely available to the public, including software running on devices or wearable technology other than smartphones, tablets, or desktop computers, the Sponsor and/or Administrator reserve the right, at their sole discretion, to require the Entrant to provide physical access to the Project hardware upon request.  

Language Requirements

All Submission materials must be in English or, if not in English, the Entrant must provide an English translation of the demonstration video, text description, and testing instructions as well as all other materials submitted. 

Team Representation

If a team or organization is entering the Hackathon, they must appoint and authorize one individual (the “Representative”) to represent, act, and enter a Submission, on their behalf. The Representative must meet the eligibility requirements above. By entering a Submission on the Hackathon Website on behalf of a team or organization you represent and warrant that you are the Representative authorized to act on behalf of your team or organization.

Intellectual Property 

Your Submission must: (a) be your (or your Team, or Organization’s) original work product; (b) be solely owned by you, your Team, your Organization with no other person or entity having any right or interest in it; and (c) not violate the intellectual property rights or other rights including but not limited to copyright, trademark, patent, contract, and/or privacy rights, of any other person or entity. An Entrant may contract with a third party for technical assistance to create the Submission provided the Submission components are solely the Entrant’s work product and the result of the Entrant’s ideas and creativity, and the Entrant owns all rights to them. An Entrant may submit a Submission that includes the use of open source software or hardware, provided the Entrant complies with applicable open source licenses and, as part of the Submission, creates software that enhances and builds upon the features and functionality included in the underlying open source product. By entering the Hackathon, you represent, warrant, and agree that your Submission meets these requirements.

Financial or Preferential Support 

A Project must not have been developed, or derived from a Project developed, with financial or preferential support from the Sponsor or Administrator. Such Projects include, but are not limited to, those that received funding or investment for their development, were developed under contract, or received a commercial license, from the Sponsor or Administrator any time prior to the end of Hackathon Submission Period. The Sponsor, at their sole discretion, may disqualify a Project, if awarding a prize to the Project would create a real or apparent conflict of interest.

 

5. Submission Modifications

Draft Submissions 

Prior to the end of the Submission Period, you may save draft versions of your submission on Devpost to your portfolio before submitting the Submission materials to the Hackathon for evaluation. Once the Submission Period has ended, you may not make any changes or alterations to your Submission, but you may continue to update the Project in your Devpost portfolio.

Modifications After the Submission Period

The Sponsor and Devpost may permit you to modify part of your Submission after the Submission Period for the purpose of adding, removing or replacing material that potentially infringes a third party mark or right, discloses personally identifiable information, or is otherwise inappropriate. The modified Submission must remain substantively the same as the original Submission with the only modification being what the Sponsor and Devpost permits. 

 

6. Judges & Criteria

Eligible submissions will be evaluated by a panel of judges selected by the Sponsor in its sole and absolute discretion (the “Judges”). Judges may be employees of the Sponsor or third parties, may or may not be listed individually on the Hackathon Website, and may change before or during the Judging Period. Judging may take place in one or more rounds with one or more panels of Judges, at the discretion of the sponsor. 

Stage One) The first stage will determine via pass/fail whether the ideas meet a baseline level of viability, in that the Project reasonably fits the theme and reasonably applies the required APIs/SDKs featured in the Hackathon.

Stage Two) All Submissions that pass Stage One will be evaluated in Stage Two based on the following equally weighted criteria (the “Judging Criteria”):

Entries will be judged on the following equally weighted criteria, and according to the sole and absolute discretion of the judges:

Technological Implementation:

Does the project demonstrate quality software development? Does the project leverage the JetBrains IDEs or AI Coding Agent Junie (encouraged)? How is the quality of the code?

 

Design:

Is the user experience and design of the project well thought out?

 

Potential Impact:

How big of an impact could the project have on the specific community or target audience?

 

Quality of the Idea:

How creative and unique is the project?

 

The judges will score each criterion out of five (5) points for a maximum total of twenty (20) points. The scores from the Judges will determine the potential winners of the applicable prizes. The Entrant(s) that are eligible for a Prize, and whose Submissions earn the highest overall scores based on the applicable Judging Criteria, will become potential winners of that Prize.

Most Valuable JetBrains Software or Junie Feedback Submission Criteria

Enter by submitting your feedback through your Devpost submission form. Eligible Feedback Submissions will be evaluated based on the completeness, viability, and potential impact of the feedback. Sponsor reserves the right to choose any one feedback submission as the winner.

Best Written Blog Post Submission Criteria

Enter by submitting your blog post link to your Devpost submission form. Eligible Blog Post Submissions may be posted on any public platform and must be publicly accessible. Sponsor reserves the right to choose any one post as the winner.

Tie Breaking 

For each Prize listed below, if two or more Submissions are tied, the tied Submission with the highest score in the first applicable criterion listed above will be considered the higher scoring Submission. In the event any ties remain, this process will be repeated, as needed, by comparing the tied Submissions’ scores on the next applicable criterion. If two or more Submissions are tied on all applicable criteria, the panel of Judges will vote on the tied Submissions.

 

7. Intellectual Property Rights

All Submissions remain the intellectual property of the individuals or organizations that developed them. By submitting an entry, entrants agree that the Sponsor will have a fully paid, non-exclusive license to use such entry for judging the entry. Entrants agree that the sponsor and Devpost shall have the right to promote the Submission and use the name, likeness, voice and image of all individuals contributing to a Submission, in any materials promoting or publicizing the Hackathon and its results, during the Hackathon Period and for three years thereafter.  Some Submission components may be displayed to the public. Other Submission materials may be viewed by the sponsor, Devpost, and judges for screening and evaluation. By submitting an entry or accepting any prize, entrants represent and warrant that (a) submitted content is not copyrighted, protected by trade secret or otherwise subject to third party intellectual property rights or other proprietary rights, including privacy and publicity rights, unless entrant is the owner of such rights or has permission from their rightful owner to post the content; and (b) the content submitted does not contain any viruses, Trojan horses, worms, spyware or other disabling devices or harmful or malicious code.

IMPORTANT NOTES ON MULTIPLE PRIZE ELIGIBILITY:

An eligible project can only win one (1) prize.

 

Substitutions & Changes: Prizes are non-transferable and may not be substituted by the winner. Sponsor in its sole discretion has the right to make a prize substitution of equivalent or greater value. Sponsor will not award a prize if there are no eligible Submissions entered in the Hackathon, or if there are no eligible Entrants or Submissions for a specific prize.

Odds: The odds of winning depend on the number of eligible entries. 

Verification Requirement: Potential winners will be notified of their selection by email. It is Entrant’s sole responsibility to configure Entrant’s settings to be able to accept notifications from Sponsor and/or Administrator. THE AWARD OF A PRIZE TO A POTENTIAL WINNER IS SUBJECT TO VERIFICATION OF THE IDENTITY, QUALIFICATIONS AND ROLE OF THE POTENTIAL WINNER IN THE CREATION OF THE SUBMISSION. No Submission or Entrant shall be deemed a winning Submission or winner until their post-competition prize affidavits have been completed and verified, even if prospective winners have been announced verbally or on the competition website. The final decision to designate a winner shall be made by the Sponsor and/or Administrator. 

Prize Delivery: Prizes will be payable to the Entrant, if an individual; to the Entrant’s Representative, if a Team; or to the Organization, if the Entrant is an Organization. It will be the responsibility of the winning Entrant’s Representative to allocate the Prize among their Team or Organization’s participating members, as the Representative deems appropriate. A monetary Prize will be mailed to the winning Entrant’s address (if an individual) or the Representative’s address (if a Team or Organization), or sent electronically to the Entrant, Entrant’s Representative, or Organization’s bank account, only after receipt of the completed winner affidavit and other required forms (collectively the “Required Forms”), if applicable. The deadline for returning the Required Forms to the Administrator is ten (10) business days after the Required Forms are sent. Failure to provide correct information on the Required Forms, or other correct information required for the delivery of a Prize, may result in delayed Prize delivery, disqualification of the Entrant, or forfeiture of a Prize. Prizes will be delivered within 60 days of the Sponsor or Devpost’s receipt of the completed Required Forms. In the event of any disqualification and/or forfeiture, Sponsor may select alternative winners.

GDC and Travel: As set forth in the table above, each winner of the Category Prizes will receive a Festival Pass ticket to the Game Developers Conference (GDC) 2026 in San Francisco, California (“GDC Event Ticket”), as well as a round-trip flight to and from San Francisco, California and a room in a hotel in San Francisco, California, with the specific hotel and number of nights (up to five (5) nights) determined by Sponsor in its sole discretion (the “All Expense Paid Trip to GDC (Flight & Hotel),” and collectively with the GDC Event Ticket, the “GDC Prizes”). The GDC Prizes are subject to the following: (1) each such winner will receive only one (1) set of GDC Prizes, even if the winner is a Team or Organization, in which case the Team or Organization must select one (1) individual member of the Team or Organization who will receive the set of GDC Prizes; (2) the winner must provide Sponsor with the name and code of the airport selected by the winner for the round-trip flight and any other information reasonably required for Sponsor to book the flight and hotel; (3) the winner must confirm the winner’s ability to attend GDC; and (4) after receiving the required information from the winner, Sponsor will book the flight and hotel and provide the winner with the relevant flight and hotel information as well as the GDC Event Ticket. Each winner is solely responsible for obtaining any visas or any other authorizations (if needed) to enter the United States. If a winner cannot attend GDC (or, if the winner is a Team or Organization, no member from the Team or Organization can attend GDC) for any reason, including failure to obtain the required visas or other authorizations to enter the United States, the winner will not be eligible for and will forfeit the GDC Prizes but may remain eligible for and may receive the remaining Prizes subject to these Official Rules and Sponsor’s sole discretion.

Fees & Taxes: Winners (and in the case of Team or Organization, all participating members) are responsible for any fees associated with receiving or using a prize, including but not limited to, wiring fees or currency exchange fees. Winners (and in the case of Team or Organization, all participating members) are responsible for reporting and paying all applicable taxes in their jurisdiction of residence (federal, state/provincial/territorial and local). Winners may be required to provide certain information to facilitate receipt of the award, including completing and submitting any tax or other forms necessary for compliance with applicable withholding and reporting requirements. United States residents may be required to provide a completed form W-9 and residents of other countries may be required to provide a completed W-8BEN form. Winners are also responsible for complying with foreign exchange and banking regulations in their respective jurisdictions and reporting the receipt of the Prize to relevant government departments/agencies, if necessary. The Sponsor, Devpost, and/or Prize provider reserves the right to withhold a portion of the prize amount to comply with the tax laws of the United States or other Sponsor jurisdiction, or those of a winner’s jurisdiction.

You will be bound by and comply with these Official Rules and the decisions of the Sponsor, Administrator, and/or the Hackathon Judges which are binding and final in all matters relating to the Hackathon.

You release, indemnify, defend and hold harmless the Promotion Entities, and their respective parent, subsidiary, and affiliated companies, the Prize suppliers and any other organizations responsible for sponsoring, fulfilling, administering, advertising or promoting the Hackathon, and all of their respective past and present officers, directors, employees, agents and representatives (hereafter the “Released Parties”) from and against any and all claims, expenses, and liabilities (including reasonable attorneys’ fees), including but not limited to negligence and damages of any kind to persons and property, defamation, slander, libel, violation of right of publicity, infringement of trademark, copyright or other intellectual property rights, property damage, or death or personal injury arising out of or relating to an Entrant's entry, creation of Submission or entry of a Submission, participation in the Hackathon, acceptance or use or misuse of the Prize (including any travel or activity related thereto) and/or the broadcast, transmission, performance, exploitation or use of the Submission as authorized or licensed by these Official Rules. 

Without limiting the foregoing, the Released Parties shall have no liability in connection with:
